Any words, even Quranic phrases, nullify prayer if the speaker intends them as a reply to someone.

Invalidators of Prayer: Speech, Crying, and Event-Based Nullifiers
Elaborates invalidators: crying, tashmit, responses, and events

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which speech acts, crying, and events invalidate the prayer according to the Hanafi school, explain the reasoning and intention-based distinctions, and apply the general prohibition of speech to specific scenarios.

Core Idea
In prayer, dhikr becomes kalam if intended as a human response.

In this lesson, we study the detailed rulings from Nur al-Idah and its commentary on what invalidates prayer. The key distinction is between actions that are considered human speech (kalam al-nas) and those that are genuine dhikr or expressions of humility. The hadith 'No human speech is suitable in prayer' serves as the central proof. We will explore crying, responding to sneezes, answering questions, and a set of event-based invalidators, noting where the Hanafi school differs internally and why intention matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Start with the hadith: 'La yasluhu fiha shay'un min kalam al-nas.' This establishes that any human speech invalidates prayer, but dhikr and Quran recitation are exceptions. The commentator expands: even utterances that resemble Quran can become kalam if intended as a response.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
2
Analyze crying and emotional sounds
Crying that produces letters (huruf) invalidates if from pain or calamity, because it communicates human distress like speech. But crying from fear of Paradise or Hell is valid as it increases khushu'. Groaning (anin) follows the same rule.
The author uses the principle that indication (dalalah) acts like explicit speech when no explicit contradicts.
3
Examine tashmit and intentional responses
Saying 'Yarhamukallah' to a sneezer invalidates according to Abu Hanifa because it is a conventional response (kalam al-nas). Abu Yusuf disagrees, considering it du'a. The resolution: if intended as response, it invalidates; if intended as dhikr, it does not. Similarly, answering 'La ilaha illallah' to a question about a rival god invalidates unless intended as mere praise.
The same logic applies to responses to good/bad news and expressions of wonder.
4
Review event-based invalidators
The passage lists several events that invalidate if they occur before sitting for tashahhud: seeing water by a mutayammim, completion of wiping period, removing khuffs, an ummi learning a verse, a naked person finding covering, ability to bow after ima', remembering a missed fard prayer, appointing an unfit imam, sunrise during fajr, and midday during 'eid. These are time-sensitive nullifiers.
The rule is that if the event occurs before the final sitting (qad qa'da qadr al-tashahhud), the prayer is invalid; after sitting, it may be valid or require repetition.
5
Synthesize the ruling with the intention condition
The common thread: any utterance or act that communicates with others or indicates a change in the person's excuse invalidates if done intentionally and before the sitting. Intention (qasd) distinguishes kalam from dhikr.
The madhhab dispute on tashmit and answering about a rival god turns on whether the utterance is inherently kalam or becomes so by intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وارتفاع بكائه من وجع أو مصيبة لا من ذكر جنة أو دار وتشميت عاطس بيرحمك الله وجواب مستفهم عن ند بلا إله إلا الله وخبر سوء بالاسترجاع وسار بالحمد لله وعجب بلا إله إلا الله أو بسبحان الله وكل شيء قصد به الجواب (و) يفسدها (ارتفاع بكائه وهو أن يحصل به حروف وقوله: (من وجع) بجسده (أو مصيبة) بفقد حبيب أو مال متعلق بالأنين وما بعده فهو قيد راجع للمسائل الأربع في الفساد لأنه إذا حصل شيء منها لأحدهما صار كأنه يقول أنه مريض فاعذروه أو مصاب فعزوه والدلالة تعمل عمل الصريح إن لم يكن صريح يخالفها ولو أفصح به تفسد فكذا هذا و (لا) تفسد بحصول هذه الأشياء الأنين وما بعده (من ذكر جنة أو نار) اتفاقاً لدلالته على زيادة الخشوع والخاشع سمي به الخائف من الواحد القهار ولا لحم على بدنه فكأنه يابس كأرض خاشعة وفي الحديث: «من أطاع الله باكياً دخل الجنة ضاحكاً ومن أذنب ذنباً ضاحكاً دخل النار باكياً» (و) يفسدها (تشميت) بالشين المعجمة أفصح من المهملة وهو الدعاء له بالخير (عاطس بيرحمك الله) أبي حنيفة وقال أبو يوسف لا تفسد لأنه دعاء بالمغفرة والرحمة كما لو قال العاطس الحمد لله على أصح الروايتين وإذا لم يرد به الجواب بل الثواب لا تفسد بالاتفاق وكذا لا تفسد لو قال غيره الحمد لله وأراد به الجواب لأنه لم يتعارف جواباً وقيل تفسد إن أراد الجواب ومحل الخلاف فيما إذا لم يرد به التفهيم فلو أراده تفسد صلاة السامع القائل الحمد لله لأنه تعليم الغير من غير حاجة وجه قول أبي حنيفة ما روينا من قوله: «إن هذه الصلاة لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس» الحديث قاله لقائله أي لتشميت معاوية بن الحكم ولأنه يجري في مخاطبات الناس فكان من كلامهم (و) يفسدها (جواب مستفهم عن ند) الله سبحانه أي قال قائل هل مع الله إله آخر فأجابه المصلي بـ: لا إله إلا الله فسدت صلاته عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف هو يقول أنه ثناء بصيغته فلا يتغير بعزيمته ولهما أنه أخرجه مخرج الجواب وهو صالح له لأنه يستعمل في موضعه عرفاً فيجعل جواباً لأن الكلام يبنى على قصد المتكلم فإن من رأى رجلاً اسمه يحيى وبين يديه كتاب فقال يا يحيى خذ الكتاب بقوة وأراد خطابه لم يشكل على أحد أنه متكلم لا قارئ (و) أمثاله ويفسدها جواب (خبر سوء بالاسترجاع) وهو قوله إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون (و) يفسدها جواب مخبر بخبر سار بالحمد لله (و) جواب خبر (عجب بلا إله إلا الله أو) جوابه (بسبحان الله ويفسدها كل شيء) مما يشبه ألفاظ القرآن إذا (قصد به الجواب) ك: يا يحيى خذ الكتاب ورؤية متيمم ماء وتمام مدة ماسح الخف ونزعه وتعلم الأمي آية ووجدان العاري ساتراً وقدرة المومي على الركوع والسجود وتذكر فائتة لذي ترتيب واستخلاف من لا يصلح إماماً وطلوع الشمس في الفجر وزوالها في العيدين (ك: يا يحيى خذ الكتاب لمن طلب كتاباً أو غيره من المصلي واستأذنه في أخذه وقوله آتينا غداءنا مستفهم عن الإتيان به تلك حدود الله فلا تقربوها نهياً لمن استأذنه في أخذ شيء عنده والخيل والبغال والحمير لمن سئل عما عنده من الماشية والوجه ما بيناه وإذا لم يرد به الجواب بل أراد إعلام أنه في الصلاة لا تفسد صلاته بالاتفاق (و) يفسدها (رؤية متيمم ماء قدر على استعماله قبل قعوده قدر التشهد كما ستفيد به المسائل التي بعد هذه أيضاً وكذا تبطل لو رآه المقتدي بمتيمم ولم يره إمامه لعلمه أن إمامه قدر بإخباره فتبطل صلاته دون صلاة الإمام لعدم قدرته وكذا تبطل بزوال كل عذر أباح التيمم قبل القعود قدر التشهد لظهور الحدث السابق كما قدمناه في التيمم (و) كذلك (تمام مدة ماسح الخف) وتقدم بيانها (و) كذا (نزعه) أي الخف سواء كان بعمل يسير أو كثير لأن هذا فيما قبل القعود قدر التشهد والاحتراز بالعمل القليل عن الكثير فيما إذا قعد قدر التشهد في الخلافية وتعلم الأمي آية الأمي منسوب إلى أمة العرب وهي الأمة الخالية عن العلم والكتابة والقراءة سواء تعلمها بالتلقي أو تذكرها بعد النسيان والتفصيل إذا قعد قدر التشهد والكلام هنا كالكلام فيما قبله وهذا إذا لم يكن مقتدياً بقارئ والمقتدي به يمضي على صلاته في الصحيح لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة فلم يتغير حال آخرها أولها ووجدان العاري ساتراً يلزمه الصلاة فيه فخرج نجس الكل ومملوك الغير إذا لم يبح له الصلاة فيه وقدرة المومي على الركوع والسجود لقوة باقيها فلا يبنى على ضعيف وتذكر فائتة لذي ترتيب والفساد موقوف فإن صلى خمساً متذكراً تلك الفائتة وقضاها قبل خروج وقت الخامسة بطلت الخمس وكذا لو قضاها بعد شيء منها بطل وصف ما صلاه قبله فصار نفلاً وإذا لم يقض المتروكة حتى خرج وقت الخامسة مما صلاه متذكراً للفائتة ارتفع الفساد واستخلاف من لا يصلح إماماً كأمي ومعذور وطلوع الشمس في الفجر لطرو الناقض في خلال ما لزم كاملاً وزوالها أي الشمس في صلاة العيدين لفوات شرط صحتها وهو وقت الضحى
And raising his voice in crying due to pain or calamity, not from mentioning Paradise or Hell, and responding to a sneezer with 'May Allah have mercy on you', and answering someone who asks about a rival god with 'There is no god but Allah', and responding to bad news with 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un', and good news with 'Alhamdulillah', and wonder with 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Subhanallah', and anything intended as a response. (And) it invalidates (raising his voice in crying which produces letters, and his statement: (from pain) in his body (or calamity) due to loss of a beloved or wealth related to groaning, and what follows is a restriction referring to the four issues of invalidity; because if any of these occurs for one of them, it becomes as if he is saying 'I am sick, excuse me' or 'afflicted, console me', and indication works like explicit statement if no explicit statement contradicts it, and if he were explicit it would invalidate, so likewise this. And (it) does not invalidate due to these things—groaning and what follows—(from mentioning Paradise or Hell) by agreement, because it indicates increased humility, and the humble one is called fearful of the One, the Subduer, and he has no flesh on his body, so he is dry like a submissive earth. In the hadith: 'Whoever obeys Allah while crying will enter Paradise laughing, and whoever commits a sin while laughing will enter Hell crying.' (And) it invalidates (tashmit) - with the dotted shin is more eloquent than the undotted - and it is supplication for good for (a sneezer saying 'May Allah have mercy on you') according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said it does not invalidate because it is a supplication for forgiveness and mercy, like if the sneezer said 'Alhamdulillah' according to the sounder of the two narrations. And if he does not intend response but reward, it does not invalidate by agreement. Likewise, it does not invalidate if someone else said 'Alhamdulillah' intending response, because it is not conventionally a response. And some said it invalidates if he intends response. The place of dispute is when he does not intend to make understand; if he intends it, it invalidates the prayer of the listener who says 'Alhamdulillah' because it is teaching others without need. The proof of Abu Hanifa's statement is what we narrated from his statement: 'Indeed this prayer is not suitable for anything of the speech of people' - the hadith he said to the one who said it, i.e., for tashmit of Mu'awiyah ibn al-Hakam, and because it occurs in people's conversations, so it is from their speech. (And) it invalidates (answering someone who asks about a rival god) - i.e., someone said 'Is there another god with Allah?' and the praying person answered with 'La ilaha illallah', his prayer is invalid according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf who says it is praise in its form, so it is not changed by his intention. And according to them, he brought it as an answer, and it is suitable for it because it is used in its place customarily, so it is made an answer; because speech is based on the intention of the speaker. Verily, if one sees a man named Yahya with a book in front of him and says, 'O Yahya, take the book with force' intending to address him, it is not doubtful to anyone that he is a speaker, not a reader. (And) the like of it, and it invalidates (answering bad news with istirja') which is his saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un.' (And) it invalidates answering a reporter of good news with 'Alhamdulillah', (and) answering news of wonder with 'La ilaha illallah' or answering it with 'Subhanallah', and it invalidates (everything) resembling Quranic phrases if (intended as response), like: 'O Yahya, take the book.' And seeing water by a mutayammim, and completion of the period of one wiping over khuffs, and removing them, and an ummi learning a verse, and a naked person finding a covering, and the ability of one performing ima' to bow and prostrate, and remembering a missed prayer for one bound by order, and appointing a substitute who is not suitable as an imam, and sunrise during Fajr, and its decline in the two 'Eid prayers. (Like: 'O Yahya, take the book' for someone who requested a book or other item from the praying person and sought permission to take it, and his statement 'Bring us our morning meal' as a question about bringing it, 'These are the limits of Allah, do not approach them' as a prohibition for one who sought permission to take something with him, and 'Horses, mules, and donkeys' for one asked about what he has of livestock. The correct view is what we explained. And if he does not intend response but intends to inform that he is in prayer, his prayer does not invalidate by agreement. (And) it invalidates (seeing water by a mutayammim who can use it before sitting for the amount of tashahhud), as will also be understood from the issues after this. Likewise, it is invalidated if a follower of a mutayammim sees it and his imam does not see it, because he knows his imam is able by his report, so his prayer is invalidated but not the imam's due to his lack of ability. Likewise, it is invalidated by removal of any excuse that permitted tayammum before sitting for the amount of tashahhud, due to the appearance of the previous impurity, as we presented in tayammum. (And) likewise (completion of the period of one wiping over the khuff) and its explanation has preceded. (And) likewise (removing it), i.e., the khuff, whether with little or much action, because this is before sitting for the amount of tashahhud. The reservation by little action from much action is when he sat for the amount of tashahhud in the difference. (And) learning of a verse by an ummi: al-ummi is attributed to the nation of the Arabs, which is the nation devoid of knowledge, writing, and reading, whether he learns it by receiving or remembers it after forgetfulness. The detail is when he sat for the amount of tashahhud, and the speech here is like the speech before it. And this is if he is not following a literate (imam). The follower continues his prayer in the correct view, because the imam's recitation is his recitation, so the state of its end does not change from its beginning. (And) a naked person finding a covering that obligates him to pray in it, so it excludes entirely impure and property of others if permission to pray in it is not given. (And) ability of one performing ima' to bow and prostrate, due to the strength of his remaining ability, so it is not built upon weakness. (And) remembering a missed prayer for one bound by order, and invalidity is suspended. If he prays five prayers remembering that missed one, and then makes it up before the time of the fifth leaves, the five are invalidated. Likewise, if he makes it up after something from it, the description of what he prayed before it becomes invalid, so it becomes supererogatory. And if he does not make up the missed one until the time of the fifth leaves, from what he prayed while remembering the missed one, the invalidity is removed. (And) appointing as substitute one who is not suitable as an imam, like an ummi or excused one. (And) sunrise during Fajr, due to the occurrence of the invalidating factor during what was required completely. (And) its decline, i.e., the sun, in the two 'Eid prayers, due to loss of the condition of its validity, which is the time of forenoon.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, discussing various speech- and event-based invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salah). The author expands on each ruling with conditions and intra-Hanafi disagreements.

The passage begins with crying (bukaa') that produces letters (huruf). If a person cries from pain or calamity, such that he produces articulated sounds, the prayer is invalidated because it communicates human distress, acting like speech. However, crying from the fear of Paradise or Hell does not invalidate, as it increases khushu' (humility) and is considered dhikr. A hadith is cited to encourage crying in obedience.

Next, tashmit (responding to a sneeze by saying 'Yarhamukallah') is discussed. Abu Hanifa rules it invalidates the prayer because it is human speech (kalam al-nas). Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing it is a supplication (du'a') and thus similar to dhikr. The author notes that if one does not intend response but reward, it is valid by agreement. The proof for Abu Hanifa is the hadith: 'This prayer is not suitable for anything of the speech of people,' which was said regarding tashmit.

Answering a question about a rival god (nad) with 'La ilaha illallah' is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), but Abu Yusuf considers it praise (thana') and thus valid. The majority argue intention matters: if the phrase is uttered as a response to a question, it becomes human speech, not dhikr. An analogy is given of saying 'O Yahya, take the book' as a command versus as recitation.

Similarly, responding to bad news with istirja' (Inna lillah), to good news with alhamdulillah, to wonder with la ilaha illallah or subhanallah, all invalidate if intended as a response. The general principle: anything resembling Quranic phrases invalidates if intended as a response to someone.

The passage then lists other invalidators: seeing water by a mutayammim before sitting for tashahhud, completion of the wiping period for khuffs, removing khuffs, an ummi learning a verse, a naked person finding covering, an ima' performer gaining ability to bow, remembering a missed prayer (for those bound by order), appointing an unfit imam, sunrise during Fajr, and noon decline during 'Eid prayers. These are all events that nullify the prayer before completing the required sitting (qad qa'da qadr al-tashahhud). Each is explained briefly with reference to previous discussions.

Key Terms
تشميت (tashmīt): Responding to a sneezer by saying 'Yarhamukallah' (may Allah have mercy on you).
إسترجاع (istirjā‘): Saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' upon hearing bad news.
أمي (ummī): A person who cannot read or write, particularly unable to recite Qur'an properly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does saying 'Yarhamukallah' to a sneezer invalidate the prayer?
A) It is a form of supplication and therefore disturbs the prayer.
B) It is considered human speech (kalam al-nas) because it is a conventional response.
C) It breaks the sequence of rak'ahs.
D) It is only invalid if said loudly.

Key Takeaway
In prayer, utterances that would be dhikr become invalidating speech if intended as a human response; similarly, events indicating change of excuse invalidate if they occur before the final sitting.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Invalidators of Prayer: Mufsidat al-Salat
List of invalidators with Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major invalidators of prayer in the Hanafi school and apply the condition that most invalidators only apply if they occur before sitting for the tashahhud.

Core Idea
Actions that nullify the excuse for tayammum, wiping, or remove consciousness invalidate the prayer when they occur before the final tashahhud.

The text from the commentary on Nur al-Idah provides a comprehensive list of events that invalidate prayer. While some invalidators are obvious, like speaking intentionally, others are subtle, such as a mutayammim seeing water. Understanding the condition that most invalidators only matter before sitting for tashahhud is key to applying these rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalidator
For each item listed, state the action or event that invalidates prayer.
Examples: seeing water, completion of wiping period, learning a verse, etc.
2
Check the timing condition
Most invalidators only nullify the prayer if they occur before the worshipper sits for the tashahhud (i.e., before the end of the prayer). Note which invalidators are conditional.
The commentary repeatedly mentions 'before sitting for tashahhud'.
3
Recognize exceptions and details
Some invalidators have additional conditions: for a mutayammim, he must be able to use the water; for the khuff, removal can be with little or much action; for the ummi, learning a verse includes remembering after forgetting; for the naked person, the covering must be pure and owned; for the mumi, the ability must be real; for the person remembering a missed prayer, the ruling depends on whether he prays it before the fifth prayer's time expires.
These details prevent misapplication.
4
Distinguish between intentional and involuntary invalidators
Some invalidators, like speech or intentional hadath, are actions of the worshipper; others, like seeing water or sunrise, are external events. The ruling applies regardless of intention if the condition is met.
This highlights the objective nature of many invalidators.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario involving one of the invalidators, determine whether the prayer is invalidated, considering timing and conditions.
Use the checklist from the guided path.

ك: يا يَحْيَى خُذِ الكِتَابَ. ورؤية متيمم ماء، وتمام مدة ماسح الخف، ونزعُهُ، وَتَعَلَّمُ الأُمِّيِّ آيَةً، وَوَجَدَانُ العاري ساتِراً وقُدْرَةُ المومِي على الركوع والسجودِ، وتَذَكَّرُ فائتة لذي ترتيب، واستخلاف منْ لا يَصْلُحُ إماماً، وطلوع الشمس في الفجر ، وزَوالُها في العيدين.
(ك: يا يحيى . (1) خذ الكتاب لمن طلب كتاباً، أو غيره من المصلي واستأذنه في أخذه، وقوله: آتينـا غداءنا مستفهم عن الإتيان به تلك حدود الله فلا تقربوها نهياً لمن استأذنه في أخذ شيء عنده، والخيل والبغال والحمير، لمن سئل عما عنده من الماشية، والوجه ما بيناه، وإذا لم يرد بـه الجواب، بل أراد إعلام أنه في الصلاة لا تفسد صلاته بالاتفاق. (و) يفسدها (رؤية متيمـم مـاء قـدر علـى استعماله قبل قعوده قدر التشهد، كما ستفيد به المسائل التي بعد هذه أيضاً، وكذا تبطل لـو رآه المقتدي بمتيمم، ولم يره إمامه؛ لعلمه أن إمامه قدر بإخباره؛ فتبطل صلاته دون صلاة الإمـام لـعــدم قدرته، وكذا تبطل بزوال كل عذر أباح التيمم ) قبل القعود قدر التشهد؛ لظهور الحدث السابق، كمـا قدمناه في التيمم)، (وَ) كذلك (تمام مدّة ماسح الخُفَّ) وتقدم بيانها، (وَ) كذا (نَزْعُهُ) أي: الخف سواء كان بعمل يسير أو كثير؛ لأن هذا فيما قبل القعود قدر التشهد، والاحتراز بالعمل القليل عن الكثير فيما إذا قعد قدر التشهد في الخلافية، وتَعَلَّمُ الأُمِّي آية). الأمي: منسوب إلى أمة العرب، وهي: ا : الأمة الخالية عن العلم والكتابة والقراءة، سواء تعلمها بالتلقي أو تذكرهـا بعـد النسيان، والتفصيل إذا قعد قدر التشهد، والكلام هنا كالكلام فيما قبله، وهذا إذا لم يكن مقتدياً بقارئ، والمقتدي به يمضي على صلاته في الصحيح؛ لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة فلم يتغير حال آخرها أولها، ووجدَانُ العاري سَاتِراً) يلزمه الصلاة فيه، فخرج نجس الكل ومملوك الغير، إذا لم يبح له الصلاة فيه، (وقُدْرَةُ المُومِي على الركوع والسجودِ)؛ لقوة باقيها، فلا يبنى على ضعيف، (وتَذَكَــرُ فائتة لذي ترتيب)، والفساد موقوف، فإن صلى خمساً متذكراً تلك الفائتة، وقضاها قبل خروج وقــــت الخامسة بطلت الخمس، وكذا لو قضاها بعد شيء منها بطل وصف ما صلاه قبله، فصار نـفــلا، وإذا لم يقض المتروكة حتى خرج وقت الخامسة مما صلاه متذكراً للفائتة ارتفع الفساد، واستخلافُ من لا يَصْلُحُ إماماً كأمي ومعذور، وطلوع الشمس في الفجر ) لطرو الناقض في خلال مـا لــزم كـاملاً، (وزَوالُها ) أي: الشمس (في) صلاة العيدين)؛ لفوات شرط صحتها وهو وقت الضحى
ودخولُ وقتِ العصر في الجمعةِ، وسُقُوطُ الجَبيرة عن بُرْء وزوالُ عُذرِ المعدُورِ، وَالحَدَثُ عَمْداً، أَوْ بِصُنْعِ غيره، والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة بنظر، أو احتلام. ومُحاذاة المشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة، مُشتركة تحريمة، في مكان متحد، بلا حائل
( ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة) لفوات شرطها ووقت الظهر، وسُقُوطُ الجَبيرة عن بُـرء) لظهور الحدث السابق وزوالُ عُذرِ ) المبيح للمسح وزوال عذر (المعذور) بنحــو سـلـس بــول، وتقدم أن شرط زواله خلو وقت كامل عنه، فتبطل به الصلاة التي انقطع في خلالها ثم استمر منقطعاً حتّـى مضى وقت کامل ، والحَدَثُ عَمْداً احترز به عن سبق الحدث، فإنه لا يبطلها، ولـه البنـاء كـمـا سنذكره) ، (أو) الحدث ( بِصُنْعِ غيره) كضربة، ووقوع ثمرة من شجرة فأدماه، (والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة) الحاصلة ( بنظر، أو احتلام)؛ بأن نام متمكناً قبله، (ومحاذاة المشتهاة)؛ ولـو في الماضي، كالعجوز الشوهاء، في أداء ركن على ما قاله محمد، أو مقداره عـلـى قول أبي يوسف، والمراد أن تحاذي رجلاً بساقها وكعبها في الأصح، ولو كانت محرماً له، أو زوجة، ولا معتبر بالسن الصغير، إنما العبرة بالضخامة والعبالة (۳) لتكون صالحة للجماع فتحاذيه (في صلاة مطلقة) هي: ذات الركوع والسجود، ولو كان بالإيماء، فلا تبطل صلاة الجنازة، (مُشتَرَكَةٍ تحريمة) المستلزم للاشتراك تأدية، والاشتراك يتحقق باتحاد فرضهما، وارتباط صلاتهما بابتناء تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، أو يكون هو إماماً لها، في مكان متحد حتى لو كان إحداهما على دكان) والآخـــر على الأرض، والدكان قدر قامة الرجل لا تفسد صلاته، لاختلاف المكان) (بلا حائل) بينهما مثل
Kaf: O Yahya, take the Book. And a mutayammim seeing water, and the completion of the period of the one wiping the khuff, and removing it, and an ummi learning a verse, and a naked person finding a covering, and the ability of the one gesturing to perform bowing and prostration, and remembering a missed prayer for one bound by order, and appointing as imam one who is not suitable, and sunrise during Fajr, and its decline during the two Eid prayers. (The commentary explains each.)
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah lists and explains the invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer. The author begins with the matn listing each invalidator, then provides commentary. The first invalidator is speaking during prayer, such as saying 'O Yahya, take the Book' (a Qur'anic verse) with the intention of answering someone – this invalidates the prayer. Then, for a mutayammim, if he sees water before sitting for the tashahhud (i.e., before the end of the prayer) and is able to use it, his prayer is invalidated because the excuse for tayammum has ceased. Similarly, if a follower of a mutayammim imam sees water, his prayer is invalidated if he informs the imam, but the imam's prayer remains valid. Completion of the duration of wiping over the khuff also invalidates prayer if it occurs before sitting for tashahhud, as does removing the khuff (whether by little or much action). An ummi (illiterate person) who learns a verse – whether by hearing or remembering after forgetting – invalidates his prayer if he does so before sitting for tashahhud. A naked person finding a cover that he must wear (i.e., pure and owned by him) invalidates his prayer if he does not cover himself. A person praying with gestures (mumi) becoming able to perform actual bowing and prostration (e.g., if his illness lifts) invalidates his prayer. Remembering a missed prayer for one who is obligated to observe order (tartib) – if he prays five daily prayers while remembering the missed one, and then prays the missed one before the time of the fifth expires, all five are invalidated; if he prays the missed one after some of them, the description of the earlier ones changes to nafl (supererogatory). Appointing an imam who is not fit (like an ummi or excused person) invalidates the prayer if done knowingly. Sunrise during Fajr prayer invalidates it because a condition (time) was lost. The sun's decline (zawal) during Eid prayers invalidates them because the condition of the time (forenoon) is lost. Entering the time of Asr during Jumu'ah invalidates the Jumu'ah prayer because its condition (time of Zuhr) is lost. The falling off of a jabeera (bandage) after healing invalidates the prayer due to the underlying hadath (state of impurity) becoming apparent. Removal of the excuse of a ma'dhur (e.g., someone with chronic urine leakage) invalidates his prayer if a complete prayer time passes without the excuse. Intentional hadath (breaking wudu) invalidates the prayer, as does hadath caused by another (e.g., being struck). Fainting and insanity invalidate the prayer because they remove consciousness. Becoming junub by looking (with desire) or wet dream invalidates the prayer because it requires ghusl. Alignment (muhadha) of a desirable woman (mushthah) – i.e., a woman capable of sexual intercourse – with the man during a shared congregational prayer with the same opening takbir, in the same place, without a barrier, invalidates the man's prayer if they are side by side, because it disturbs the order of the congregation. The commentary clarifies conditions like the woman being past the age of desire, not necessarily young, and the alignment being such that their bodies are adjacent.

Key Terms
مفسدات الصلاة (mufsidat al-salat): Actions or events that nullify the prayer, requiring its repetition if done intentionally or knowingly.
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to lack of water or excuse.
مسح الخف (mash al-khuff): Wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) as a substitute for washing feet in wudu.
أمي (ummi): A literal illiterate person, one who cannot read or write.
مشتهاة (mushthah): A woman who is desirable for sexual intercourse; typically one who has reached puberty and is not too old.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person who prays with gestures (mumi) becomes able to perform actual bowing and prostration during the prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer remains valid if he continues gesturing.
C) He must change to actual movements and the prayer continues.
D) He can choose between gestures and actual movements.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies a comprehensive set of invalidators of prayer, most of which nullify the prayer only if they occur before sitting for the tashahhud, highlighting the importance of timing and conditions.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Invalidators of Prayer: Muhadhat and Other Nullifiers
Listing invalidators with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the invalidators of prayer and apply the nine conditions for muhadhat to determine whether a prayer is invalidated.

Core Idea
Muhadhat invalidates only with specific conditions: absolute prayer, shared takbir, same place, no barrier, and imam's intention.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the events that nullify a valid prayer (mufsidat) and provides detailed conditions, especially for the alignment of a desirable woman (muhadhat). Understanding these conditions protects against unnecessary nullification and ensures correct application of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall category
First, list the invalidators of prayer mentioned in the passage. These include: entering Asr time during Jumu'ah, falling off of splint, removal of excuse, intentional hadath or by another, fainting, insanity, janabah from looking or wet dream, and muhadhat. Note that each has conditions and exceptions.
The passage focuses on the conditions for muhadhat, but other invalidators are listed.
2
Focus on muhadhat conditions
Identify the specific conditions for muhadhat to be invalidating: the prayer must be absolute (with ruku' and sujud), shared in takbirat al-ihram (same obligation and linked to imam), in a single place, without a barrier, and the woman must be mushtahāt (desirable). Additionally, the imam must have intended her imamate.
There is also the condition that the woman's limb aligns with the man's shin and ankle.
3
Analyze the barrier and gap rules
Examine what constitutes a barrier: the width of a man's back and thickness of a finger. A gap equivalent to the space of a praying person also serves as a barrier. If the imam gestures but the woman does not move back, her prayer is invalidated but not his.
The barrier must be present throughout the alignment.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note the difference between Muhammad (requires performance of a rukn) and Abu Yusuf (requires the amount of a rukn) regarding the duration of alignment. Also, the ninth condition about the imam's intention: most require specific intention for Jumu'ah and Eid, while some say absolute imamate suffices.
This ikhtilaf affects whether the prayer is invalidated or not.
5
Consider other invalidators and exceptions
Review other invalidators and their exceptions: e.g., preceding hadath does not invalidate if one builds upon the prayer; fainting and insanity invalidate but certain excuses allow building; passing nearby water to go further invalidates unless the distance is short.
The passage provides many exceptions to preserve the prayer where possible.

ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة، وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء وزوال عذر المعذور، والحدث عمداً، أو بصنع غيره، والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة بنظر، أو احتلام. ومحاذاة المشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة، مشتركة تحريمة، في مكان متحد، بلا حائل. ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة لفوات شرطها ووقت الظهر، وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء لظهور الحدث السابق وزوال عذر المبيح للمسح وزوال عذر المعذور بنحو سلس البول، وتقدم أن شرط زواله خلو وقت كامل عنه، فتبطل به الصلاة التي انقطع في خلالها ثم استمر منقطعاً حتى مضى وقت كامل، والحدث عمداً احترز به عن سبق الحدث، فإنه لا يبطلها، وله البناء كما سنذكره، أو الحدث بصنع غيره كضربة، ووقوع ثمرة من شجرة فأدماه، والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة الحاصلة بنظر أو احتلام بأن نام متمكناً قبله، ومحاذاة المشتهاة ولو في الماضي كالعجوز الشوهاء، في أداء ركن على ما قاله محمد، أو مقداره على قول أبي يوسف، والمراد أن تحاذي رجلاً بساقها وكعبها في الأصح، ولو كانت محرماً له أو زوجة، ولا معتبر بالسن الصغير، إنما العبرة بالضخامة والعبالة لتكون صالحة للجماع فتحاذيه في صلاة مطلقة هي ذات الركوع والسجود ولو كان بالإيماء، فلا تبطل صلاة الجنازة، مشتركة تحريمة المستلزم للاشتراك تأدية، والاشتراك يتحقق باتحاد فرضهما، وارتباط صلاتهما بابتناء تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، أو يكون هو إماماً لها، في مكان متحد حتى لو كان إحداهما على دكان والآخر على الأرض، والدكان قدر قامة الرجل لا تفسد صلاته لاختلاف المكان، بلا حائل بينهما مثل مؤخرة الرجل في الطول وغلظ الإصبع، فإن كان لا تضر المحاذاة لأن أدنى الأحوال القعود فقدر الحائل بقدره، والفرجة تقوم مقام الحائل وأدناها قدر ما يقوم فيه المصلي، ولم يشر إليها لتتأخر، فإن أشار إليها فلم تتأخر هي فسدت صلاتها دون صلاته لإتيانه بما في وسعه، وتقدمه عنها بالمشي مكروه، فإذا ترك الإشارة فسدت بالمحاذاة صلاته. والتاسع من شروط المحاذاة المفسدة أن يكون الإمام قد نوى إمامتها لأنه شرط لصحة اقتدائها كما قدمناه، فإذا لم ينوها لا تفسد محاذاتها، وفي الجمعة والعيدين قال أكثرهم لا يصح أيضاً اقتداؤها ما لم ينو إمامتها بالخصوص، وقال بعضهم يصح اقتداؤها فيهما لأن الإمام ينوي مطلق الإمامة، ويفسدها ظهور عورة من سبقه الحدث في ظاهر الرواية ولو اضطر إليه للبناء على ما مضى من صلاته ككشف المرأة ذراعها للوضوء بعد سبق حدثها وهو الصحيح إلا أن يكون انكشافاً كثيراً في زمن يسير دون أداء ركن كقلبه كما قدمناه، وقراءته أي قراءة من سبقه الحدث في حالة كونه ذاهباً للوضوء أو عائداً للوضوء، أما في الذهاب فلإتيانه بركن القراءة مع منافي الصلاة وهو الحدث، وأما في حال عوده متوضئاً فلأدائه الركن مع المنافي وهو المشي، واحترز بقراءته عن التسبيح فإذا سبح لا تفسد صلاته على الأصح لأنه ليس من أجزائها، ومكثه قدر أداء ركن بعد سبق الحدث مستيقظاً بلا عذر، حتى لو كان نائماً متمكناً في الصلاة فرعف ومكث نائماً ثم انتبه فإنه يبني، أو مكث لعذر الزحام أو يرفع لسيلان الرعاف إلى أن ينقطع يبني، وإذا سبقه الحدث راكعاً أو ساجداً لا يرفع رأسه بقصد إتمام الركن تحرزاً عن إفساد الصلاة بذلك بل يرفع رأسه ناوياً البناء ويتأخر محدودباً للستر ثم ينصرف للطهارة، ومجاوزته ماء قريباً لغيره أي لما أبعد من غير عذر النسيان ونحوه، إلا إذا كان الماء القريب في بئر أو مجاوزه قليلاً قدر صفين كما إذا وجد مشرعة من الماء فتركها وذهب إلى أخرى بجنبها، وفيه إشارة إلى أن فعل ما يحتاج إليه لا يضره.
And the entering of the time of Asr in Jumu'ah prayer, and the falling off of the splint after healing, and the removal of the excuse of the one with an excuse, and intentional hadath, or by the action of another, and fainting, and insanity, and janabah by looking or wet dream. And the alignment of a desirable woman in an absolute prayer, shared in takbirat al-ihram, in a single place, without a barrier. The entering of Asr time in Jumu'ah is due to the loss of its condition and the time of Zuhr. The falling off of the splint after healing is due to the appearance of the previous hadath. The removal of the excuse of the one with an excuse is like urinary incontinence, and it was previously mentioned that its removal requires a complete time free from it, so the prayer in which it interrupted during and then continued intermittently until a complete time passed becomes invalid. Intentional hadath distinguishes from preceding hadath, which does not invalidate, and he may build upon it as we will mention. Hadath by the action of another, like a blow or a falling fruit that causes bleeding. Fainting, insanity, and janabah resulting from looking or a wet dream, by sleeping securely before it. The alignment of a desirable woman, even if in the past like an ugly old woman, for the performance of a rukn according to Muhammad, or the amount of it according to Abu Yusuf. The meaning is that she aligns with a man by her shin and ankle in the most correct view, even if she is his mahram or wife. Consideration is not by young age, but by bulk and corpulence so that she is fit for intercourse, so she aligns with him. In an absolute prayer, which is one with bowing and prostration, even if by gestures, so the funeral prayer is not invalidated. Shared in takbirat al-ihram necessitates sharing in performance, and sharing is realized by the unity of their obligation and the connection of their prayers by the dependence of their ihrams on the ihram of the imam, or he is her imam. In a single place, such that if one is on a raised platform and the other on the ground, and the platform is the height of a man, his prayer is not invalidated due to the difference of place. Without a barrier between them like the back of a man in length and thickness of a finger; if there is, alignment does not harm because the minimum state is sitting, so the barrier is estimated accordingly. A gap stands in place of a barrier, and its minimum is the space occupied by a praying person. He did not gesture to her to move back; if he gestured and she did not move back, her prayer is corrupted but not his, because he did what he could, and for him to move ahead by walking is disliked. If he did not gesture, his prayer is corrupted by alignment. The ninth condition of the corrupting alignment is that the imam must have intended her imamate, because it is a condition for the validity of her following, as we previously mentioned. If he did not intend it, her alignment does not corrupt. In Jumu'ah and the two Eids, most said that her following is not valid unless he intends specifically her imamate, and some said it is valid because the imam intends absolute imamate. And it invalidates it: the appearance of the private part of one who had a preceding hadath in the apparent narration, even if he is forced to uncover for building upon his previous prayer, like a woman uncovering her arm for wudu after her hadath passed, which is the correct view, unless the uncovering is significant in a short time without performing a rukn, like its opposite as we mentioned. And his recitation, meaning the recitation of the one who had a preceding hadath while going for wudu or returning from wudu. As for going, because he performs the rukn of recitation with something that contradicts the prayer, namely hadath. As for when he returns after wudu, because he performs the rukn with something that contradicts it, namely walking. He distinguished recitation from tasbih; if he performs tasbih, it does not invalidate his prayer in the most correct view because it is not part of its integral parts. And his staying for the duration of performing a rukn after a preceding hadath while awake without excuse, even if he was sleeping securely in the prayer and had a nosebleed and remained sleeping then woke up, he may build upon it. Or if he stayed due to crowding or to stop the nosebleed until it stops, he builds. If hadath preceded him while bowing or prostrating, he does not raise his head intending to complete the rukn to avoid corrupting the prayer, but raises his head intending to build and moves back hunched over for concealment, then leaves for purification. And his passing by nearby water to go to further water without excuse of forgetfulness or the like, except if the nearby water is in a well or the passing is a short distance like two rows, as if he finds a drinking place and leaves it for another beside it. This indicates that doing what is necessary does not harm him.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer, as explained in the commentary of Nur al-Idah. The author lists several events that nullify a valid prayer, each with detailed conditions. These invalidators include: the entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah prayer (because the condition of Jumu'ah and the time for Zuhr are lost), the falling off of a splint after healing (revealing the previous state of hadath), the removal of an excuse like urinary incontinence (when a full time period passes without discharge), intentional hadath (distinguishing from unintentional prior hadath which allows building upon the prayer), hadath caused by another, fainting, insanity, janabah from looking or a wet dream (provided the person slept securely), and the alignment (muhadhat) of a desirable woman. The conditions for muhadhat to be invalidating are detailed: the prayer must be an 'absolute prayer' with bowing and prostration (not funeral prayer), shared in takbirat al-ihram (same obligation and linked to imam), in a single place without a barrier. The barrier is defined as the width of a man's back and a finger's thickness; a gap equivalent to a praying person's space also prevents invalidation. If the imam gestures for a woman to move back and she does not, her prayer is corrupted but not his. Additionally, the imam must have specifically intended her imamate for the alignment to corrupt; in Jumu'ah and Eid, most scholars require specific intention. Other invalidators include: the appearance of a private part after a preceding hadath (even if forced, like a woman uncovering her arm for wudu during building), recitation by someone who had a preceding hadath while going or returning from wudu (since walking contradicts prayer), staying awake for the duration of a rukn after a preceding hadath without excuse, and passing by nearby water to go to further water without a valid excuse. In all cases, exceptions and conditions are given to preserve the validity of the prayer where possible.

Key Terms
المشتهاة (al-mushtahāt): A woman who is sexually desirable, whether currently (like a nine-year-old) or in the past (like an old woman), as per the context of muhadhat.
محاذاة (muhādhāh): The alignment of a woman's body with a man's body during prayer, specifically when their limbs are parallel, which invalidates the prayer under certain conditions.
صلاة مطلقة (ṣalāh muṭlaqah): An absolute prayer that includes bowing and prostration, as opposed to funeral prayer (janazah) which does not have these postures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) If he is praying in congregation with a shared imam.

Key Takeaway
Alignment of a desirable woman invalidates a man's prayer only when eight conditions are met, including the imam's specific intention; otherwise, the prayer remains valid.

The Ninth Condition for Invalidating a Woman's Prayer by Alignment: Imam's Intention and Barrier Size
Explains the ninth condition for invalidity: imam's intention, and the barrier size

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ninth condition for a woman's alignment to invalidate her prayer, explain why the imam's intention is required, and describe the minimal barrier size that prevents invalidation.

Core Idea
A woman's alignment invalidates her prayer only if the imam intended to lead her and no sufficient barrier exists.

In this lesson, we examine the specific conditions that make a woman's alignment with the imam invalidate her prayer. The text clarifies the ninth condition—the imam's intention—and also details the minimal size of a barrier (ḥāʼil) that prevents invalidation. We will also note an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning Jumuʻah and ʻEid prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a woman aligning (muḥādhāh) with the imam during prayer. Under certain conditions, her prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The text lists several conditions, focusing on the ninth.
2
List the conditions for invalidation
The passage mentions: the imam's intention, appearance of private parts, recitation while going for wudu, staying after hadath, passing water, and the barrier size. We focus on the ninth: intention.
Other conditions are listed but not expanded.
3
Understand the rationale for intention
The imam must have intended to lead the woman because it is a condition for the validity of her following (iqitida). Without intention, her alignment does not invalidate.
4
Examine the barrier size
The minimal barrier is the back of a man's foot in length and the thickness of a finger. A gap can also serve if it is as wide as the space a praying person occupies. If the barrier is this size, alignment does not harm.
The barrier prevents invalidation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
In Jumuʻah and ʻEid, most Hanafis say the imam must specifically intend to lead the woman. Some say a general intention (absolute leadership) suffices. The majority view requires specific intention.
This affects whether the woman's prayer is valid in those prayers.

Invalidators of Prayer Due to Hadath During the Prayer
Lists invalidators when hadath overtakes: uncovering 'awra, recitation, remaining, passing water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actions that invalidate the prayer when overtaken by hadath and state the Hanafi ruling with exceptions.

Core Idea
Hadath during prayer does not automatically invalidate; only specific actions—like reciting Quran, exposing 'awra, or staying idle without excuse—cause invalidity.

When a person is overtaken by hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer, the prayer is not automatically invalid. Instead, certain actions must be avoided to maintain the prayer's validity. This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the specific invalidators and the conditions under which building (bina') is permitted. Understanding these rules helps the praying person navigate sudden impurity without losing their prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that the prayer is in progress and hadath (e.g., nosebleed, wind) occurs. The prayer is not immediately invalid; it depends on subsequent actions.
The text uses 'sabaq al-hadath' meaning the hadath overtakes the person.
2
List the four invalidators
From the passage, extract the four actions that invalidate the prayer after hadath: 1) covering 'awra unnecessarily, 2) reciting Quran while going or returning from wudu, 3) remaining idle for a pillar's duration without excuse, 4) passing by a near water source to go to a farther one without excuse.
Each invalidator is explained with exceptions.
3
Note exceptions and nuances
Understand that tasbih (glorification) does not invalidate; necessary movements (like covering 'awra for wudu) are allowed; excuses like sleep, crowding, or nosebleed cessation allow building.
The text says 'wa huwa al-sahih' for the woman's case and 'al-asahh' for tasbih.
4
Determine the ruling when building is allowed
If the person avoids invalidators, they may build upon the prayer after purification. The prayer is not lost. Examples: sleeping nosebleed victim, one stuck in crowd.
Building is allowed for 'sky-based' hadath like nosebleed; ground-based hadath typically requires restart.
5
Apply to different scenarios
Test the rules: a woman uncovering her forearm for wudu (valid since necessary), but if she uncovers excessively without a pillar, it's fine; a person reciting Quran while walking to wudu (invalid); a person staying idle for a full rukn time (invalid unless excused).
The text emphasizes intention: raising head from bowing should be for building, not completing the pillar.

(And) it invalidates it: the appearance of the private part of one whom the hadath overtook, in the apparent narration even if forced to it for building upon what passed of his prayer, like a woman uncovering her forearm for wudu after her hadath overtook her, and that is the correct view, unless it is much uncovering in a short time without performing a pillar like turning it over as we have presented, and his recitation, i.e., the recitation of one whom the hadath overtook while he is (going) for wudu or (returning) for wudu. As for going, because he performed the pillar of recitation with something contrary to prayer, which is the hadath. As for the state of his return after wudu, because he performed the pillar with something contrary, which is walking. And by his recitation he excludes tasbih, for if he does tasbih his prayer is not invalid according to the most correct view, because it is not among its parts. And his staying the extent of performing a pillar after the hadath overtook him while awake without an excuse. So if he was sleeping soundly in prayer and had a nosebleed and remained sleeping then woke up, he builds; or he remained due to the excuse of crowding, or lifts to stop the flow of nosebleed until it stops, he builds. And if the hadath overtook him while bowing or prostrating, he does not raise his head with the intention of completing the pillar to avoid invalidating the prayer thereby, rather he raises his head intending to build, and steps back hunched for covering, then goes for purification. And his passing by water near for someone else, i.e., for what is further away without an excuse of forgetfulness etc., unless the near water is in a well, or his passing is slight, the extent of two rows, as if he finds a drinking place of water and leaves it and goes to another adjacent to it. And in it is an indication that doing what he needs does not harm him.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage details the invalidators that occur when a person is overtaken by hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. According to the Hanafi school (in zahir al-riwaya), the prayer is invalidated if the person's private part becomes exposed, even if forced (as in a woman uncovering her arm for wudu). Also invalidating is reciting Quran while going to or returning from wudu after hadath, because recitation is a pillar combined with a contradictory action (hadath or walking). However, tasbih (glorification) is not invalidating as it is not part of the prayer's integral. Additionally, remaining idle for the duration of a pillar after hadath without an excuse invalidates the prayer. The text specifies exceptions: if the person was asleep, or due to crowding, or waiting for nosebleed to stop, the prayer remains valid and they may build upon it. If hadath occurs in bowing or prostration, one should raise the head intending to resume later, not to complete the pillar. Finally, passing by a near water source to go to a farther one without a valid excuse also invalidates the prayer, but slight deviation (like two rows) or if the near water is in a well is excusable. The principle is that necessary actions do not invalidate.

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (sabaq al-ḥadath): A sudden hadath (ritual impurity) that overtakes the praying person.
بناء على الصلاة (binā’ ‘alā al-ṣalāh): Continuing the prayer from where it was interrupted, rather than restarting.
مكث قدر ركن (mukth qadr rukn): Staying idle for the time it takes to perform one integral (pillar) of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Uncovering the forearm for wudu
B) Reciting the Quran while going for wudu
C) Saying subhanAllah (tasbih)
D) Remaining idle for a pillar

Key Takeaway
The prayer after hadath remains valid if the person avoids reciting Quran, exposing 'awra unnecessarily, staying idle for a pillar, or bypassing near water; otherwise, they must build upon it after purification.

Mistaken Beliefs During Prayer: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Discusses invalidators based on mistaken belief and advises restart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing corrective and rejective mistaken beliefs to determine whether a prayer is invalidated, and explain the role of istihsan in overriding strict qiyas.

Core Idea
In prayer, mistaken beliefs invalidate only if the action amounts to rejection; corrective actions preserve validity through istihsan.

This lesson explores a set of scenarios where a worshipper acts on a mistaken belief during prayer, such as thinking they have hadath or that their wudu has broken. The Hanafi school uses the principle of istihsan to preserve the prayer's validity in some cases, while classifying other actions as abandonment. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assessing the effect of honest mistakes in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of mistaken actions
Recognize that the text contrasts ẓann al-ḥadath (mistaken hadath) with other mistaken beliefs. The former is for correction, the latter for rejection. This intention determines the ruling.
Intention (niyyah) is key.
2
Understand the qiyas ruling on turning from qibla
The text states that by qiyas, turning away from the qibla invalidates the prayer absolutely. This establishes the asl (original case) that any significant deviation invalidates.
Qiyas would extend this to leaving the mosque for any reason.
3
Apply istihsan for corrective actions
Istihsan overrides qiyas when the person intends correction (qaṣd al-iṣlāḥ) and does not actually leave the mosque. The prayer remains valid because the movement is not considered abandonment.
Istihsan is a Hanafi principle that allows flexibility.
4
Distinguish other mistaken beliefs
Believing one is not in wudu, that the wiping period expired, that a missed prayer is due, or that impurity exists—these actions are performed as rejection (rafḍ). They invalidate the prayer even if the person does not leave the mosque.
The test: if the imagined scenario were true, would the person need to restart? If yes, acting on it invalidates.
5
Apply the preferred practice: restart to avoid disagreement
The text concludes that the best course in all cases of doubt is to restart the prayer absolutely (isti'nāf), to avoid the internal Hanafi disagreement on specific scenarios (e.g., returning after the imam).
This reflects the principle of iḥtiyāṭ (precaution).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲) وهو الدار والبيت والجبانة، ومصلى الجنازة. ط.
(۳) أي: لصلاة إمامه. اعلم أنه إذا كان منفرداً فالعود أفضل لتقع الصلاة في مكان واحد، وقيل: الأفضل أن لا يعود لما فيه من تقليل المشي، وكذا إن كان مقتدياً فرغ إمامه، فإن لم يفرغ وكان بينهما ما يمنع ا عليه العود، والإمام كالمقتدي في تحتم العود إن كان ثمة ما يمنع الاقتداء لتحول الإمامة عنه أفاده السيد، فالفساد في عبارة المؤلف مقيد بما إذا كان بين المقتدي والإمام ما يمنع الاقتداء. ط.

And his leaving the mosque thinking he has hadath because of the existence of a contradictory element, which is walking without excuse, and by qiyas it would invalidate by turning away from the qibla absolutely. But istihsan (juristic preference) is that it remains valid when he does not leave the mosque, because he intended correction, so it is considered as long as the place did not change. And the house, the home, the graveyard, and the funeral prayer place are like the mosque. And his passing by the rows in other than it, meaning in the desert, not in the mosque nor its ruling. And whoever prays alone in the desert, his mosque is his prostration place from the four sides, except if he walks forward and has a sutra, then what is inside it is given the ruling of the mosque. So if he exceeds that thinking he has hadath, his prayer is invalidated, as if water comes from his nose and he thinks it is blood. And similarly it is invalidated by not returning to his imam if he remains in it. But if he has finished, he has the choice between completing it in his place or returning to the first, and they differed on what is better. And some said it is invalidated by his return after his imam finished to his place. (And) it invalidates it: his departing from his station thinking he is not in wudu, or thinking that the period of his wiping has ended, or thinking that he has a missed prayer, or thinking that he has impurity, even if he did not leave the mosque in these cases, because his departing is by way of rejection and abandonment, therefore if what he imagined is realized, he would restart, contrary to thinking he has hadath, because that is not for rejection but for correction. And this is the principle. And it has been known from what we mentioned the conditions for building due to a sky-based hadath in prayer. (And) the best is to restart absolutely to avoid disagreement, due to the saying...
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage addresses invalidators that arise from acting on a mistaken belief during prayer. If a person leaves the mosque thinking he has hadath, by qiyas the prayer would be invalid due to walking away from qibla, but by istihsan it remains valid as long as he does not actually leave the mosque because he intends correction. The same ruling applies to house, home, graveyard, and funeral prayer places. When praying in the desert without a sutra, the valid space is the area of prostration; exceeding it invalidates. The text also discusses the case of a follower who thinks his imam has finished and then returns later; there is a difference of opinion on whether this invalidates. Moreover, if a person departs from his station thinking he is not in wudu, or that his wiping period ended, or that he has a missed prayer or impurity, the prayer is invalidated even if he does not leave the mosque, because this departure is an act of rejection. The fundamental principle is that actions based on mistaken belief invalidate if they amount to abandoning the prayer, but not if they are for correction. Finally, the best practice in all cases of doubt is to restart the prayer to avoid scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms
ظن الحدث (ẓann al-ḥadath): Mistakenly thinking that one has hadath (ritual impurity) when in fact one does not.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A Hanafi legal principle preferring a more flexible ruling over strict qiyas due to a stronger consideration.
استئناف (isti’nāf): Restarting the prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Restart the prayer (isti'naf)
C) Continue where you left off
D) Make a second prayer without repeating

Key Takeaway
The key principle is that mistaken beliefs only invalidate prayer when they lead to actions of rejection; corrective actions preserve validity through istihsan, but restarting is always best to avoid disagreement.

Suspicion of Hadath and Leaving Mosque During Prayer
States rulings on invalidation of prayer due to suspicion of hadath and preference for isti'naf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between invalidating and non-invalidating movements during prayer due to suspicion of hadath, and explain the Hanafi position on building (bina') vs restarting (isti'naf).

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque with suspicion of hadath invalidates prayer; but movements for repair within the same place permit building.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents the Hanafi rulings on how suspicion of ritual impurity (hadath) affects the validity of prayer. It distinguishes between actions that indicate rejection (like turning away thinking wudu is broken) and those that are for repair (like leaving the mosque to purify). The author also addresses the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, where the Hanafi school allows building (resuming) under certain conditions, but recommends restarting to avoid disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its classification
What is the act being ruled upon? Leaving the mosque, passing rows, turning away with suspicion. Determine which actions invalidate prayer.
The passage lists multiple scenarios; note which ones are considered 'rejection' vs 'repair'.
2
Locate the analogy and the istihsan override
The text mentions that by strict analogy (qiyas), any turning from the qibla would invalidate, but istihsan is applied because the intention is repair.
Understanding the role of istihsan is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the conditions for building
Building (bina') is permitted only if the person does not leave the mosque, and the action is for repair.
Places like house, courtyard, and funeral area are treated as mosque for this ruling.
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Shafi'i holds that any such action invalidates entirely; Hanafi allows building within same place. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The dispute is legitimate; both schools have evidence.
5
Evaluate the preference for isti'naf
The author says restarting is better to avoid disagreement, citing consensus vs. single report.
This shows the Hanafi method of preferring consensus (ijma) when possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروجه من المسجدِ يظنُّ الحدث، ومجاوزته الصفوف في غيره بظنه، وانصرافه ظانا أنَّه غير متوضي، أو أنَّ مُدَّةَ مَسْحِهِ انْقَضَتْ، أَوْ أَنَّ عليهِ فائتة، أو نجاسة، وإن لم يخرج من المسجد، والأفضل الاستئناف...... كالاستقاء من البئر على المختار، وخرز دلوه لو كان متخرقاً، وفتح الباب، وتكرار الغسل ثلاثاً، واستيعاب الرأس بالمسح والمضمضة، والاستنشاق ثلاثاً على الأصح؛ لأن الفـــرض يقوم بالكل، وقيل: يتوضأ مرة مرة، وإن زاد فسدت وغسل نجاسة أصابته من سبق الحدث لا مـن غـيـره، وإلقـاء الثوب المتنجس منه (١) . عنه ( وخروجه من المسجدِ يظنُّ الحدث لوجود المنافي وهـو المشـي بـغـيـر عذر، والقياس فسادها بالانحراف عن القبلة مطلقاً. ولكن الاستحسان بقاؤها عند عدم الخروج مــن المسجد؛ لأنه لقصد الإصلاح فاعتبر منه ما لم يختلف المكان، والدار، والبيت، والجبانة، ومصلى الجنازة كالمسجد، ومجاوزته الصفوف، في غيره) يعني: في الصحراء لا في المسجد ولا في حكمه (۳)، وإن مشى أمامه وليس بين يديه سترة فالصحيح هو التقدير بموضع السجود، ومـن كــان يصلي في الصحراء وحده، فمسجده موضع سجوده من الجوانب الأربع، إلا إذا مشى أمامـه وبـيـن يديه سترة فيعطى لداخلها حكم المسجد، فإذا تجاوز ذلك ( بظنّه ) أي : الحدث فسدت صلاته، كما لو نزل من أنفه ماء فظنه دماً . وكذا تفسد بعدم عوده لإمامه (۳) إن بقي فيها، وأما إن كان قد فرغ، فله الخيار بين إتمامها في مكانه أو عوده إلى الأول، واختلفوا في الأفضل، وقيل: تفسد بعوده بعد فراغ إمامه إلى مكانه، (وَ) يفسدها (انْصِرَافُهُ) عن مقامه (ظانّاً أنَّه غير متوضئ)، (أو) ظانا (أَنَّ مُدَّةَ مَسْحِهِ انْقَضَتْ، أَوْ ظاناً أنَّ عليه فائتة، أو ظاناً أن عليه نجاسة ، وإِنْ لَمْ يَخْرُجُ) في هذه الصور ( منَ المَسْجِدِ)؛ لأن الانصراف فيها على سبيل الرفض والترك، ولهذا لو تحقق ما توهمه يستقبل، بخلاف ظن الحدث، لأنه ليس للرفض بل للإصلاح، وهذا هو الأصل، وقد علم بما ذكرنا شروط البناء لسبق الحدث السماوي في الصلاة، ( والأفضلُ الاستئناف مطلقاً تحرزاً عن الخلاف، لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله ببطلانها به وعدم البناء (۱) (۱) ، وقيل : إن كان يصلي بالجماعة فالأفضل البناء، إحرازاً لفضيلة الجماعة، وإلا فالاستقبال وفي « الحافظية » و « المستصفى» الدلائل أربعة: الكتاب، و الخبر المسموع من رسول الله و و و الخبر المتواتر ، والإجماع، والمجوزة أربعة أيضاً: الآية المؤولة، والخبر الواحد، والعام المخصوص، والقياس، فلو بني يكون عملاً بخبر الواحد، ولو استأنف يكون عملاً بالإجماع فكان أولى انتهى.
And his leaving the mosque suspecting hadath, and his passing the rows in other than a mosque with suspicion, and his turning away thinking he is not in wudu, or that the period of his wiping has expired, or that he has a missed prayer, or that there is impurity, even if he did not leave the mosque, and the better is to restart... like drawing water from a well on the preferred view, and stitching his bucket if it was torn, and opening the door, and repeating the washing three times, and encompassing the head with wiping and rinsing the mouth and nose three times on the most sound view; because the obligatory duty is fulfilled by the whole, and it is said he performs wudu once each, and if he increased it becomes invalid. And washing an impurity that befell him due to preceding hadath not from other than it, and throwing away the garment that became impure from it. This is narrated from him. And his leaving the mosque suspecting hadath due to the existence of that which is incompatible (with prayer) and that is walking without excuse, and by analogy it would invalidate by turning away from the qibla absolutely. But istihsan (juristic preference) is that it remains valid when he does not leave the mosque because he intends repair, so it is considered from him as long as he does not change the place. And the house, the courtyard, the cemetery, and the funeral prayer area are like the mosque. And his passing the rows in other than a mosque (meaning in the desert, not in the mosque nor in its ruling). And if he walked in front of him and there is no sutra (barrier) in front of him, then the correct is the estimation by the place of prostration. And whoever prays in the desert alone, his mosque is the place of his prostration from the four sides, except if he walked in front of him and there is a sutra in front of him, then the inside of it is given the ruling of the mosque. So if he exceeds that with suspicion (i.e., of hadath) his prayer becomes invalid, just as if water came from his nose and he thought it was blood. And likewise it becomes invalid by his not returning to his imam if he (imam) remains in it. But if he (imam) has finished, then he has the choice between completing it in his place or returning to the first, and they differed on which is better. And it is said it becomes invalid by his returning after his imam finished to his place. And (invalidation occurs by) his turning away from his standing place thinking he is not in wudu, or thinking that the period of his wiping has expired, or thinking that he has a missed prayer, or thinking that there is impurity, even if he does not leave the mosque in these cases because the turning away in these is in the manner of rejection and abandonment, and therefore if what he presumed is true he would start anew, unlike suspicion of hadath because it is not for rejection but for repair. And this is the principle. And it has been known from what we mentioned the conditions for building due to a heavenly hadath occurring in prayer. And the better is to restart absolutely to avoid disagreement, due to the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him that it invalidates and no building. And it is said that if he prays in congregation, building is better to preserve the virtue of congregation, otherwise restarting. And in al-Hafiziyya and al-Mustasfa, the pieces of evidence are four: the Book, the heard report from the Messenger of Allah, and the mutawatir report, and consensus, and the permissibles are also four: the interpreted verse, the single report, the general that is specified, and analogy. So if he builds, he acts upon a single report, and if he restarts, he acts upon consensus, so it is more appropriate. End.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the invalidation of prayer due to suspicion of hadath. The author first states the ruling: leaving the mosque with suspicion of hadath, passing rows outside the mosque, turning away thinking one is not in wudu, or that the wiping period expired, or that there is a missed prayer or impurity – all invalidate the prayer even if one does not leave the mosque. The preferred view is to restart the prayer. The text then discusses the detail: leaving the mosque with suspicion of hadath is considered an invalidating act because it involves walking without excuse. By analogy (qiyas), any deviation from the qibla would invalidate, but the Hanafi school prefers istihsan: the prayer remains valid if the person does not leave the mosque because the movement is for repair (islah). Places like the house, courtyard, cemetery, and funeral prayer area are treated like the mosque. For a person praying alone in the desert, his 'mosque' is the area of his prostration. If he walks in front and there is a sutra, the area inside the sutra is like the mosque. Exceeding that with suspicion invalidates. The passage also covers the case of returning to the imam: if the imam is still in prayer, one must return; if the imam has finished, one has a choice. For cases of turning away with suspicion of being without wudu, etc., the prayer is invalidated because the action is a rejection, not repair. The author then notes that the better is to restart absolutely to avoid disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the prayer is invalidated without possibility of building. A quote from al-Hafiziyya and al-Mustasfa explains that building relies on a single report, while restarting relies on consensus, so restarting is more appropriate.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that breaks wudu, such as passing wind or urine.
الانحراف عن القبلة (al-inhiraf 'an al-qibla): Turning away from the direction of the Kaaba during prayer.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from the strict analogy for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person leaves the mosque during prayer due to suspicion of hadath?
A) The prayer remains valid.
B) The prayer becomes invalid.
C) The prayer becomes invalid only if the suspicion is confirmed.
D) The prayer becomes invalid but can be resumed upon return.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque with suspicion of hadath invalidates the prayer, but movements for repair within the same place allow building; restarting is preferred to avoid disagreement with Shafi'i.

Opening on Non-Imam During Prayer: Ruling and Corrective Actions
Ruling with proof on correcting recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for correcting recitation during prayer and distinguish between correcting the imam versus other individuals.

Core Idea
Correcting the imam during prayer is allowed to preserve its validity; correcting others invalidates the prayer.

One of the subtleties of Hanafi fiqh regarding prayer is the distinction between permissible and invalidating actions. The act of 'al-fath' (correcting or prompting recitation) carries different rulings depending on whom one is correcting. This lesson explores the source text from Nur al-Idah that explains when such correction invalidates the prayer and when it is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is correcting recitation (al-fath). If correcting a non-imam, the prayer is invalidated; if correcting the imam, it is allowed.
The ruling differs based on whom is corrected.
2
Understand the reason behind the ruling
Correcting a non-imam is teaching without necessity, hence invalid. Correcting the imam is necessary because the imam may inadvertently say something that invalidates the prayer.
The rationale is darura (necessity) to preserve the prayer.
3
Recognize the scope of the exception
The allowance for correcting the imam applies even after the imam's obligatory recitation or after moving to another verse.
This is on the soundest view (al-sahih).
4
Note the authoritative view
The text states 'al-sahih' (the soundest view), indicating the mufta bihi position that neither prayer is invalidated.
Some intra-Hanafi disagreement existed, but the relied-upon view is as given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يفسدها (فَتْحُهُ) أي: المصلي (عـلـى غـيـر إمامه ) لأنه تعليم لغير ضرورة، وفتحه على إمامه في إصلاح صلاته؛ لأنه قد يجري على لسانه ما يكون مفسداً، ففتحه عليه ولو بعد قراءته المفروض، أو بعد انتقاله إلى آية أخرى لا يفسد صلاته ولا صلاة الإمام ) على الصحيح
And it invalidates it: his opening (correcting) i.e., the worshipper, on other than his imam, because it is teaching without necessity. And his opening on his imam for the correction of his prayer, because something that invalidates may flow upon his tongue, so his opening on him even after his obligatory recitation or after his moving to another verse does not invalidate his prayer nor the prayer of the imam, on the soundest view.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof about opening (correcting the recitation) during prayer. The author first states that opening on someone other than the imam invalidates the prayer because it is teaching without necessity. However, opening on the imam himself for the purpose of correcting his prayer is permissible, because the imam might accidentally say something that would invalidate the prayer. The ruling applies even if the follower opens after the imam has completed his obligatory recitation or moved to another verse. This does not invalidate either the follower's prayer or the imam's prayer, according to the correct view.

Key Terms
الفتح (al-fath): Correcting or prompting the recitation of someone else during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower corrects (opens) someone other than the imam during prayer?
A) The follower's prayer is invalidated.
B) The person corrected must repeat the prayer.
C) Nothing happens, it is allowed.
D) The prayer of both is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
Correcting the imam during prayer is permissible to ensure the prayer's validity, but correcting anyone else invalidates the prayer.
