Takbir with Intention to Move to Another Prayer Invalidates
Ruling on takbir with intention to transition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on takbir with intention to move to another prayer and explain the underlying legal reasoning (qiyas).

Core Idea
Saying takbir with intention to switch prayers invalidates the current prayer because the intention to leave is confirmed by the takbir.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah discusses a specific scenario: a person who is praying and says takbir (Allahu Akbar) with the intention of moving to a different prayer. The text explains that this action invalidates the current prayer. It provides several examples to illustrate the principle and distinguishes between prayer and fasting. We will analyze the ruling and its underlying rationale through qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what specific action triggers invalidation and what the ruling is. The act is saying takbir with the intention to transition to another prayer. The ruling: the current prayer becomes fasid (invalid).
The takbir itself is a rukn for entering prayer, but when done with intention to switch, it acts as an exit.
2
Understand the rationale
Why does this invalidate? Because the intention to leave the current prayer is confirmed by the takbir, which is a definitive action. The text says: 'because his commencement in other than it is valid due to the intention of attaining what was not attained, so he exits from his prayer that he was in necessarily.'
The intention alone (without action) would not be enough; the takbir makes it operative.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The text draws several analogies: from fard to nafl, from alone to following an imam, and from a latecomer standing to make up missed rak'ahs. Each case shares the common illa: intention to leave confirmed by takbir.
The qiyas is based on the principle that a confirmed intention to exit by takbir invalidates the current prayer.
4
Note the exception
If one intends to restart the exact same prayer (e.g., to repeat it), saying takbir does not invalidate; rather, the additional rak'ahs are joined to the same prayer. However, if one deliberately leaves and sits thinking he began anew, the prayer is invalidated.
The exception shows that the intention must be to transition to a different prayer or a different status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يفسدها ( التَّكبيرُ بِنيَّة الانتقال لصلاة أخرى غير صلاته)؛ لأنه صح شروعه في غيرها لنية تحصيل ما لم يكن حاصلاً، فيخرج عن صلاته الـتـي كــان فـيـهـا ضرورة، وكذا لو كان منفرداً فنوى الاقتداء أو عكسه، وكذا لو كان مسبوقاً فقام لقضـاء مـا سـبـق بـه فشك، وكبر ينوي الاستقبال يخرج عن صلاته، لأن حكم صلاة المسبوق وحكـم صـلاة المنفرد يختلفان، ألا يرى أن الاقتداء بالمسبوق لا يصح، وبالمنفرد صحيح. فإذا أقبل على أحدهما وكبر ثبت الانتقال إلى الأخرى، كمن انتقل بالتكبير من فرض إلى نفل وعكسه، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد»، ولو كان يصلي على جنازة فجيء بأخرى فكبر ناوياً الاستئناف صار مستأنفاً للثانية، وأشرنا إلى أنه لو كبر يريد استئناف عين ما هو فيه لا يفسد به ما مضى حتى لو لم يقعـد علـى آخر ما بقي من الركعات يضمه إلى ما مضى، بل تركه وقعد على آخرها ظن أنه افتتـح بـه مـكـبراً بطلت صلاته، ومعلوم أنه لم يتلفظ بالنية، لأنه لو تلفظ بها بطل ما مضى للمنافي وهو الكلام، وقيدنا بالصلاة، لأنه لو كان صائماً عن قضاء رمضان، ثم نوى بعد الشروع افتتاح صومه لغيره لا يضر في صحة الأول، ثم قيد بطلان الصلاة فيما تقدم بـمـا ( إذا حصلت) واحدة مـن (هَـذه الـصـور
And it invalidates it: the takbir with the intention of transition to another prayer other than his prayer, because his commencement in other than it is valid due to the intention of attaining what was not attained, so he exits from his prayer that he was in necessarily. Likewise if he was alone and intended to follow (an imam) or the opposite, and likewise if he was a latecomer and stood to make up what he missed and doubted and said takbir intending to start anew, he exits from his prayer, because the ruling of the prayer of the latecomer and the ruling of the prayer of the lone worshipper differ. Do you not see that following a latecomer is not valid, but following a lone worshipper is valid? So if he turns to one of them and says takbir, the transition to the other is confirmed, like one who transitions by takbir from an obligatory to a supererogatory prayer and vice versa. Similarly in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. And if he was praying over a janaza and another was brought and he said takbir intending to restart, he becomes restarting the second. And we indicated that if he said takbir intending to restart the very same prayer he is in, it does not invalidate what has passed, even if he did not sit for the last remaining rak'ahs he joins them to what passed, but if he leaves and sits at the end of it thinking he began with it, saying takbir deliberately, his prayer is invalidated. And it is known that he did not utter the intention, because if he uttered it, what passed would be invalidated due to the incompatible action (speech). And we restricted (that to prayer) because if he was fasting for the make-up of Ramadan and then after commencing intended to start his fast for something else, it does not harm the validity of the first. Then the invalidation of prayer is restricted by what was mentioned to 'if one of these cases occurs'.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the invalidation of prayer by saying takbir with the intention to move to another prayer. The author explains that if a person says takbir intending to transition to a different prayer (e.g., from fard to nafl, or from one prayer to another), the current prayer is invalidated because the intention to leave it is established. The same applies if one changes from being alone to following an imam, or vice versa, due to the different rulings of these types of prayer. The text gives various examples: a latecomer who stands to make up missed rak'ahs and then says takbir intending to start anew invalidates his prayer; similarly, a person praying over a janaza who says takbir wanting to restart for a second janaza becomes engaged in the second. However, if one says takbir intending to restart the exact same prayer (e.g., to repeat it), it does not invalidate what passed; rather, the additional rak'ahs are joined to the previous ones. But if one deliberately leaves and sits thinking he began anew, then the prayer is invalidated. The author also notes that uttering the intention aloud would invalidate the prayer due to speech. Finally, he distinguishes between prayer and fasting: in fasting, a change of intention after commencement does not invalidate the fast, but in prayer it does.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying Allahu Akbar to begin prayer or signify transition.
النية (al-niyya): The intention in the heart for which action is performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person says takbir intending to move from an obligatory prayer to a supererogatory prayer?
A) The obligatory prayer remains valid and the supererogatory begins after.
B) Both prayers become invalid.
C) The obligatory prayer is invalidated and the supererogatory begins.
D) The person must repeat both prayers.

Key Takeaway
Saying takbir with intention to leave a prayer for another invalidates the current prayer, due to the confirmed intention to exit.

Invalidators of Prayer: Opening on a Non-Imam and Takbir with Intent to Switch
Main ruling: two invalidators of prayer with timing condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two actions that invalidate prayer and state the temporal condition that determines their effect.

Core Idea
Two invalidators of prayer: opening on a non-imam and takbir with intention to switch – only if before final sitting.

This lesson examines two specific actions that can invalidate the prayer, as stated in the Hanafi matn. Understanding the exact condition for invalidation – occurring before the final sitting – is crucial for applying the ruling correctly in practice. We will explore the legal description and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions
Locate in the text the two actions described: 'opening upon a non-imam' (reciting or correcting someone else’s prayer) and 'takbir with intention to transition to another prayer'. These are the mufsidat (invalidators).
These actions are explicitly listed in the source.
2
Recognize the ruling and exception
Understand that these actions invalidate the prayer (make it batil), but only if they occur before the final sitting of the tashahhud extent. If after, the prayer remains valid.
The condition 'before final sitting' is the key determinant.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
Take a concrete scenario: a person is in the last rak'ah and after prostrating, before sitting, he recites to correct another person. According to the text, this invalidates his prayer. If he does the same after sitting and reciting tashahhud, it does not invalidate.
The final sitting begins when the person sits after the last sajdah of the last rak'ah.
4
Differentiate from similar actions
Note that these are specific mufsidat. Other actions like laughing, eating, or turning away have different rulings and timing conditions. This lesson focuses only on these two.
Memorize the list of mufsidat from Nur al-Idah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفَتْحُهُ على غير إمامِهِ، والتكبيرُ بِنيَّةِ الانتقالِ لصلاة أخرى غير صلاتِهِ. إذا حصلت هذه. المذكوراتُ قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد
And [the prayer is invalidated by] his opening [recitation] upon someone other than his imam, and the takbir with the intention of transitioning to another prayer other than his own prayer. When this occurs, the mentioned [invalidators] [invalidate only] before the final sitting of the extent of the tashahhud.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage states two invalidators of prayer (mufsidat): (1) the praying person's recitation of al-Fatihah (or any correction) for someone other than his imam, as this constitutes teaching without necessity; (2) pronouncing takbir with the intention of leaving his current prayer for another. However, these invalidate only if they occur before the final sitting (qadr al-tashahhud), which is the amount of time needed to recite the tashahhud. If they occur after that, the prayer is considered complete and not invalidated. This is a clear ruling from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فتحه على غير إمامه (fatḥuhu ʿalā ghayri imāmihi): The praying person's act of reciting or correcting someone other than his imam, such as another congregation or individual, without necessity.
التكبير بنية الانتقال (al-takbīr bi-niyyati al-intiqāl): Pronouncing the takbir (Allahu akbar) with the intention to leave the current prayer and begin another.
قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد (qabla al-julūsi al-ākhiri miqdāra al-tashahhud): Before the final sitting of the prayer, which is the amount of time sufficient to recite the tashahhud. This is the cutoff for when certain invalidators take effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At any point during the prayer
B) Only if they occur before the final sitting of the extent of the tashahhud
C) Only if they occur after the final sitting
D) They never invalidate the prayer

Key Takeaway
Two specific invalidators of prayer – opening on a non-imam and takbir with intent to switch – only invalidate if they occur before the final sitting (al-julus al-akhir).

Building on Prayer After Hadath: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding building on prayer after hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows building on prayer after hadath, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and evaluate the strength of each school's evidence.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school relies on a specific hadith to allow building; Shafi'i qiyas is overridden by textual evidence.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a prayer can be continued (built upon) after ritual impurity (hadath) occurs. The Hanafi school, based on a direct hadith, permits building, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that any impurity nullifies the prayer entirely. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the schools prioritize different types of evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that if a person experiences hadath during prayer, they may leave, perform wudu, and resume from where they stopped. This is permitted based on a specific hadith.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that hadath invalidates the prayer completely, and one must restart. His proof is qiyas: hadath is like any deliberate nullifier (e.g., talking), which breaks the prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that a specific hadith overrides the qiyas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowed building after similar impurities. A textual proof takes precedence over analogy.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – one can continue the prayer from where stopped; Shafi'i – the entire prayer is invalid and must be restarted.
5
Understand the methodological principle
The passage also notes that the proofs for building include the Quran, mutawatir hadith, and consensus, while the opposing evidence is based on solitary report, specified general, and analogy. This shows the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi usul.
The Hanafi position is built on a specific textual proof that overrides general analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله ببطلانها به وعدم البناء (۱) (۱) ، وقيل : إن كان يصلي بالجماعة فالأفضل البناء، إحرازاً لفضيلة الجماعة، وإلا فالاستقبال وفي « الحافظية » و « المستصفى» الدلائل أربعة: الكتاب، و الخبر المسموع من رسول الله و و و الخبر المتواتر ، والإجماع، والمجوزة أربعة أيضاً: الآية المؤولة، والخبر الواحد، والعام المخصوص، والقياس، فلو بني يكون عملاً بخبر الواحد، ولو استأنف يكون عملاً بالإجماع فكان أولى انتهى.
Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, [holds] that it is invalidated by it and no building. And it is said: If he is praying in congregation, then building is preferable to obtain the virtue of congregation; otherwise, restart. And in al-Hafiziyya and al-Mustasfa: The evidences are four: the Book, the heard report from the Messenger of Allah and and and the mutawatir report, and consensus; and the permissible [evidences] are also four: the interpreted verse, the solitary report, the general text that is specified, and analogy. So if he builds, he acts upon a solitary report; if he restarts, he acts upon consensus, so it is more appropriate. End.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of building (al-bina') upon one's prayer after a hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the prayer becomes invalid and one must start over without building, because the hadath nullifies the state of purity, similar to any deliberate nullifier. However, the Hanafi school, based on a hadith, allows building after removing the impurity. The passage also quotes a view that if one is in congregation, building is preferable to preserve the congregation's virtue; otherwise restarting is better. It then mentions a methodological principle from two works: the proofs for building include the Quran, mutawatir hadith, and consensus, while the opposing proofs are the interpreted verse, solitary hadith, specified general, and analogy. The tarjih (preference) is given for building because acting on a solitary report (which supports building) is outweighed by acting on consensus (which supports restarting), but the Hanafi position is based on a different evidence chain.

Key Terms
البناء على الصلاة (al-bināʾ ʿalā al-ṣalāh): Resuming the prayer from the point of interruption after removing the cause of invalidation, without restarting the entire prayer.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): A state of ritual impurity, either minor (wudu) or major (ghusl), that nullifies prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hanafis restart the prayer; Shafi'is build
B) Hanafis build; Shafi'is restart
C) Both schools agree on building
D) Neither allows building

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits building on prayer after hadath based on a specific hadith, while the Shafi'i school requires restarting based on qiyas.

Additional Invalidators of Prayer: Madd al-Hamzah, Reading from Mushaf, Awrah/Najasah, and Muqtadi Racing
Further invalidators of prayer enumerated with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four additional invalidators of prayer listed in the passage and apply the ruling for muqtadi racing with correct conditions.

Core Idea
Four actions invalidate prayer: lengthening hamzah in takbir, reading from mushaf what you don't memorize, performing a pillar with awrah/najasah, and racing the imam without rejoining.

This passage from Nur al-Idah expands the list of prayer invalidators (mufsidat). The Hanafi school holds that these specific actions break the prayer because they introduce extraneous elements or violate the required conformity with the imam. The ruling for muqtadi racing is nuanced—it depends on whether the follower gives salam with the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first invalidator and its condition
Madd al-hamzah in the takbir (e.g., 'Allaahu akbar' with prolonged 'a') changes the meaning and invalidates the prayer.
This applies regardless of intent—the alteration of the word matters.
2
Identify the second invalidator and its limitation
Reciting from a mushaf what one does not have memorized is invalid because it involves looking and learning. If one already memorizes the passage, it is not an invalidator.
The key condition is 'ما لا يحفظه' (what he does not memorize).
3
Identify the third invalidator and its conditions
Performing a pillar (like ruku') while the awrah is uncovered or while there is a preventing impurity (najasah maniah) invalidates the prayer.
Both conditions are independent invalidators; either one suffices.
4
Analyse the muqtadi racing scenario
If a follower performs a pillar before the imam and does not repeat it with or after him, then gives salam with the imam, the prayer is invalid. If he does not give salam with the imam (having raced in all rak'ahs), he must make up one rak'ah without recitation.
The follower is considered a 'lahiq' (latecomer) who missed the first rak'ah by not following the imam's ruku'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفسدها أيضاً مدُّ الهمزة في التكبيرِ، وقراءة ما لا يَحْفَظُهُ من مصحف، وأداء ركن أو إمكانه، مع كشفِ العَوْرَةِ، أو مع نجاسة مانعة، ومسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه إمامه، كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام ولم يعده معه أو بعده، وسلم مع الإمام، أما إذا لم يسلم مع الإمام، وقد أتـي بالركوع والسجود قبله في كل الركعات، فإنه يلزمه قضاء ركعة بلا قراءة؛ لأن مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لاحق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام، وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع
And it is also invalidated by: elongating the hamzah in the takbir, and reciting what he does not memorize from a mushaf, and performing a pillar or its possibility with uncovering of the awrah, or with a preventing impurity, and the muqtadi's racing ahead in a pillar in which his imam did not participate with him—such as if he bowed and raised his head before the imam and did not repeat it with him or after him, and he gave salam with the imam. But if he did not give salam with the imam, and he performed ruku' and sujud before him in every rak'ah, then he must make up a rak'ah without recitation; because one who catches the first part of the imam's prayer is a lahiq, and he makes up before the imam finishes, and he missed the first rak'ah by abandoning following the imam in ruku'.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage lists additional invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer. First, elongating the hamzah in the takbir (e.g., saying 'Allaahu akbar' with excessive prolongation) changes the meaning. Second, reading what one does not memorize from a written copy of the Quran (mushaf) involves looking and learning, which is extraneous. Third, performing a prayer pillar (rukn) like ruku' while the awrah is uncovered or with a preventing najasah (impurity) invalidates. Fourth, a muqtadi (follower) racing ahead of his imam in a pillar (e.g., bowing before the imam) without rejoining invalidates. The text explains the ruling for a muqtadi who bows and rises before the imam: if he gives salam with the imam, his prayer is invalid; but if he does not give salam, having done all ruku' and sujud before the imam in every rak'ah, he must make up one rak'ah without recitation because he is a 'lahiq' (latecomer) and missed the first rak'ah by not following the imam in the ruku' of that rak'ah.

Key Terms
مسابقة المقتدي بركن (musābaqat al-muqtadī bi-rukn): The follower's act of performing a pillar (e.g., ruku') before the imam does, without repeating it with him or after.
مد الهمزة (madd al-hamzah): Elongating the sound of the hamzah in the takbir (e.g., 'Allah' with a prolonged 'a'), which changes the word's meaning.
قراءة من مصحف (qirā'ah min muṣḥaf): Reciting from a written copy of the Quran during prayer, if one does not have the passage memorized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) His prayer is invalid
C) He must repeat the ruku' after the imam
D) He must make up a rak'ah with recitation

Key Takeaway
Four specific actions invalidate prayer; the ruling for muqtadi racing depends on whether he gives salam with the imam.

Is Exiting Prayer a Fard? Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions on whether exiting prayer is obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the status of exiting prayer and identify the mufta bihi view, explaining its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Exiting prayer is wajib, not fard; al-Karkhi dismisses the fard claim as a misderivation.

When an invalidator occurs just before the salam, after the final sitting, does the prayer become invalid or remain valid? This hinges on a deeper question: Is the very act of exiting the prayer (khuruj) a fard obligation? Within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa's statements were interpreted to mean it is fard, but the Sahibayn and later authorities hold it is only wajib. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context and consensus
The passage first notes agreement that invalidators before the final sitting break the prayer. The dispute only applies after the final sitting (qadr al-tashahhud).
The final sitting of tashahhud is the key boundary.
2
State the two positions within Hanafism
One view (attributed to Abu Hanifa via al-Barda'i) says exiting is fard, so if an invalidator occurs after the final sitting without having exited, prayer becomes invalid. The Sahibayn say exiting is not fard, so the prayer remains valid.
No explicit text from Abu Hanifa himself — al-Barda'i deduced it.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's proof
If exiting were fard, it would require a specific act of worship, like salam or takbir. But exiting can occur through speech or hadath (impurity), which are not acts of worship. Therefore, exiting is not fard.
4
Examine al-Karkhi's critique
Al-Karkhi refutes the deduction: Abu Hanifa's statements about invalidation are explained by the unity of the prayer, not by considering exiting a fard. He asserts the school consensus that exiting is not fard.
Al-Karkhi strengthens the Sahibayn's position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
If someone speaks deliberately after the final sitting, according to the Sahibayn prayer is valid (since exiting is not fard). The mufta bihi is that exiting is wajib, not fard, and the prayer is valid. This is the relied-upon position.
The practical difference: whether to repeat the prayer or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذكورات قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد فتبطل بالاتفاق. وأما إذا عَرضَ المنافي قبيل السلام بعد القعود قدر التشهد فالمختار صحة الصلاة؛ لأن الخروج منها بفعل المصلي واجب على الصحيح، وقيل: تفسد بناء على ما قيل أن الخروج بصنعه فرض عند الإمام لا عندهما، ولا نص فيه عن الإمام، وإنما أخذه أبو سعيد البردعي من قول الإمام بفساد الصلاة، في هذه المسائل فقال: إن الصلاة لا تفسد إلا بترك الفرض، ولم يبق في هذه الصور إلا الخروج بصنعه، فإذا فسدت بتركه كان فرضاً، وعندهما: الخروج بفعل المصلي ليس فرضاً؛ لأنه لو كان كذلك لتعين بما هو قربة، كسائر واجبات الصلاة، فلما صح الخروج بالكلام والحدث دل على أنه ليس بفرض، فإذا حدثت هذه العوارض ولم يبق عليه فرض صار كما بعد السلام، وقال الكرخي: لا خلاف بين أصحابنا في أن الخروج من الصلاة بفعل المصلي ليس بفرض، وغلط البردعي في استنباط فريضته على قول الإمام من المسائل المذكورة؛ لأنه لو كان فرضاً لاختص بما هو قربة وهو السلام، ولما لم يختص علمنا أنه ليس بفرض، وإنما قال الإمام أبو حنيفة ببطلان الصلاة في هذه المسائل؛ لأن ما يغير الصلاة في أثنائها يغيرها في آخرها كنية الإقامة واقتداء المسافر بالمقيم انتهى. وقول الكرخي: بأن تعمد المغير في آخرها ليس كهو قبله، فلا يصح إلحاقه به، على أنه معقول في مقابلة منقول وهو غير مقبول انتهى.
The mentioned [invalidators] before the final sitting of the extent of the tashahhud invalidate by consensus. As for when an invalidator occurs close to the salam after sitting of the extent of the tashahhud, the chosen position is the validity of the prayer; because exiting from it by the action of the prayer is obligatory (wajib) according to the sound view. And it is said: it is invalidated based on what is said that exiting by his own action is a fard according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), not according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And there is no text from the Imam about it; rather Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i took it from the Imam's statement of the invalidation of prayer in these issues. He said: Prayer is only invalidated by leaving a fard, and nothing remains in these forms except exiting by his own action. So if it becomes invalid by leaving it, it is fard. According to the two companions: exiting by the action of the worshipper is not fard; because if it were so, it would have been specified with what is an act of worship, like other obligations of prayer. Since exiting by speech or hadath is valid, it indicates it is not fard. So when these invalidators occur and no fard remains, it becomes like after salam. Al-Karkhi said: There is no dispute among our companions that exiting from prayer by the worshipper's action is not fard, and he rebuked al-Barda'i for deriving its fardiyya from the Imam's statement in the mentioned issues; because if it were fard, it would be specific to what is an act of worship, i.e., salam. Since it is not specific, we know it is not fard. Rather, Imam Abu Hanifa said prayer is invalidated in these issues because what changes the prayer in its middle changes it in its end, like the intention of iqama and the following of a traveler by a resident. End. And the statement of al-Karkhi that deliberate change at the end is not like before it, so analogy to it is not valid, although it is rational in opposition to transmitted, is not accepted. End.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of exiting prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah). The issue arises when an invalidator occurs close to the end of the prayer, after the final sitting of the tashahhud. The consensus is that if the invalidator occurs before the final sitting, the prayer is invalid. But if it occurs after, the chosen position is that the prayer remains valid. The reasoning involves whether exiting the prayer by the worshipper's own action (e.g., saying salam) is a fard (obligation) or not. Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i deduced from statements of Abu Hanifa that exiting is a fard: because if prayer is invalidated by leaving it, then it must be obligatory. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that exiting is not a fard, because if it were, it would have to be done with a specific act of worship like salam, but other actions like talking or hadath can also exit the prayer, proving it is not fard. Al-Karkhi further clarifies that there is no real dispute: all Hanafis agree that exiting is not fard, and al-Barda'i's derivation is mistaken. The Imam's ruling on invalidation in certain cases is based on unity of the prayer, not on the fardiyya of exiting.

Key Terms
الخروج من الصلاة (al-khurūj min al-ṣalāh): The act of ending the prayer by the worshipper's own action, such as salam or intentional speech.
فرض (farḍ): An obligatory element of prayer that, if omitted, requires repetition or prostration of forgetfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a fard (obligatory) element
B) It is not fard; the prayer can be exited by various actions
C) It is a sunnah
D) It is haram to exit other than by salam

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that exiting prayer is wajib, not fard, meaning any permissible action after the final sitting completes the prayer and an invalidator afterward does not nullify it.

Nullifiers After Final Sitting: A Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer nullifiers after final tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on nullifiers after the final sitting and evaluate the reasoning of al-Barda'i versus al-Karkhi.

Core Idea
Exiting prayer is wajib, so a nullifier after the final sitting does not invalidate.

A worshipper who has completed the final tashahhud and is about to say salam may suddenly do something that normally invalidates prayer, like speaking. Does the prayer become invalid? The Hanafi school has an internal debate on this. This lesson walks through the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa's followers and the reasoning that leads to the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
Determine the issue: whether a nullifier (e.g., talking) occurring after the final sitting (julus akhir) but before salam invalidates the prayer.
The final sitting is of the duration of tashahhud.
2
State the two opposing views
One view (attributed to al-Barda'i) says the prayer is invalid; the other (Sahibayn and al-Karkhi) says it remains valid. The chosen view (mukhtar) is validity.
3
Analyze the proof for validity
The proof: exiting prayer by one's own action is wajib, not fard. If it were fard, it would be specified as an act of worship (like salam). Since it can be done by anything (speech, etc.), it is not fard. Therefore, when a nullifier occurs, no fard remains, so the prayer is not invalidated.
4
Examine the opposing argument
Al-Barda'i argues that because Imam Abu Hanifa invalidated prayer in similar cases (like changing intention), exiting must be fard. But al-Karkhi refutes this, saying there is no explicit text from the Imam, and the analogy from the middle of prayer to its end is invalid.
5
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the prayer is valid. This is the view of the Sahibayn and the later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذكوراتُ قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد، ويفسدها أيضاً مدَّ الهمزة في التكبيرِ، وقراءة ما لا يَحْفَظُهُ من مصحف، وأداء ركن أو إمكانه، مع كشفِ العَوْرَةِ، أو مع نجاسة مانعة، ومسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه إمامه . ( المذكورات قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد فتبطل بالاتفاق. وأما إذا عَرَضَ المنافي قبيل السلام بعد القعود قدر التشهد فالمختار صحة الصلاة؛ لأن الخروج منها بفعل المصلي واجب على الصحيح، وقيل: تفسد بناء على ما قيل أن الخروج بصنعه فرض عند الإمام لا عندهما، ولا نص فيه عن الإمام، وإنما أخذه أبو سعيد البردعي من قول الإمام بفساد الصلاة، في هذه المسائل فقال: إن الصلاة لا تفسد إلا بترك الفرض، ولم يبق في هذه الصور إلا الخروج بصنعه، فإذا فسدت بتركه كان فرضاً، وعندهما: الخروج بفعل المصلي ليس فرضاً؛ لأنه لو كان كذلك لتعين بما هو قربة، كسائر واجبات الصلاة، فلما صح الخروج بالكلام والحدث دل على أنه ليس بفرض، فإذا حدثت هذه العوارض ولم يبق عليه فرض صار كما بعد السلام، وقال الكرخي: لا خلاف بين أصحابنا في أن الخروج من الصلاة بفعل المصلي ليس بفرض، وغلط البردعي في استنباط فريضته على قول الإمام من المسائل المذكورة؛ لأنه لو كان فرضاً لاختص بما هو قربة وهو السلام، ولما لم يختص علمنا أنه ليس بفرض، وإنما قال الإمام أبو حنيفة ببطلان الصلاة في هذه المسائل؛ لأن ما يغير الصلاة في أثنائها يغيرها في آخرها كنية الإقامة واقتداء المسافر بالمقيم انتهى. وقول الكرخي: بأن تعمد المغير في آخرها ليس كهو قبله، فلا يصح إلحاقه به، على أنه معقول في مقابلة منقول وهو غير مقبول انتهى. وفيه تأمل
The things mentioned before the final sitting (of the extent of the tashahhud) – and it [the prayer] is also invalidated by prolonging the hamza in the takbir, and reading from a mushaf what one does not memorize, and performing a pillar or the possibility of it while the awrah is exposed or with an impurity that prevents, and the muqtadi racing ahead in a pillar in which his imam did not accompany him. (The things mentioned before the final sitting of the extent of the tashahhud – then it [the prayer] is invalidated by agreement. But if a contradicting occurrence appears right before the salam after the sitting of the extent of the tashahhud, then the chosen view is that the prayer is valid; because exiting it by the action of the worshipper is wajib according to the correct view. And it was said: it is invalidated based on what was said that exiting by his own action is fard according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], not according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and there is no text from the Imam about it. It is only that Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i took from the Imam's statement of invalidation of prayer in these issues and said: The prayer is only invalidated by leaving a fard, and in these situations nothing remains except exiting by his own action. So if it is invalidated by leaving it, it was fard. According to the two, exiting by the action of the worshipper is not fard; because if it were so, it would have to be specified with what is an act of worship, like other obligatory acts of prayer. Since exiting by speech and nullifying acts is valid, it indicates that it is not fard. So when these occurrences happen and no fard remains upon him, it becomes like after the salam. Al-Karkhi said: There is no disagreement among our companions that exiting the prayer by the action of the worshipper is not fard, and al-Barda'i erred in deducing its being fard from the Imam's statement from the mentioned issues; because if it were fard, it would be specific to what is an act of worship, which is the salam, and since it is not specific, we know it is not fard. The Imam Abu Hanifa only said the prayer is invalid in these issues because that which changes the prayer during it changes it at its end, like the intention for iqamah and the traveler following a resident. And the statement of al-Karkhi: that intentionally changing at its end is not like before it, so it is not correct to analogize it to it, despite it being rational in contrast to transmitted, which is not acceptable. And there is reflection upon it.)
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether nullifiers (such as talking or any act that contradicts prayer) that occur right before the concluding salam, after having performed the final sitting for the duration of the tashahhud, invalidate the prayer. The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that the prayer is valid. The reasoning is that exiting the prayer by one's own action (such as saying salam) is wajib, not fard. Since the only remaining obligation is exiting, and that is wajib, a nullifier does not invalidate. This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Some, like Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i, argued that according to Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on certain similar cases, exiting by one's own action is fard, so a nullifier would invalidate. However, al-Karkhi refutes this, stating that there is consensus among the Hanafis that exiting by one's own action is not fard. The passage notes that there is no explicit text from Imam Abu Hanifa on this specific point. The author then cites al-Karkhi's objection to analogizing the end of prayer to its middle. The discussion is left with a note of reflection (fihi ta'ammul), indicating that the matter is nuanced.

Key Terms
الجلوس الأخير (al-julus al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer after the last rak'ah, during which the tashahhud is recited.
الخروج بفعل المصلي (al-khuruj bi-fi'l al-musalli): Exiting the prayer state by the worshipper's own act (e.g., saying salam or any deliberate action).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (al-mukhtar) in this passage, if a person speaks after the final sitting but before salam, what is the status of their prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid.
C) The prayer is makruh.
D) It requires repetition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mukhtar position is that a nullifier after the final sitting does not invalidate prayer, because exiting is wajib, not fard.

Prolonging the Hamza in Takbir Invalidates Prayer
Ruling on a specific nullifier of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that intentionally prolonging the hamza in the takbir invalidates the prayer and explain why.

Core Idea
Prolonging the hamza in 'Allahu Akbar' changes the pronunciation and invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a specific nullifier of prayer: prolonging the hamza in the takbir. The author notes that this was discussed earlier, but here it is listed as an invalidator. Understanding the precise conditions is important to avoid nullifying the prayer inadvertently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that prolonging the hamza in the takbir (e.g., saying 'Allaaaah' instead of 'Allah') is a deliberate change in pronunciation.
This applies to any prolongation that alters the meaning or adds an extra letter.
2
State the ruling
The prayer is invalidated (batil) by this act because it changes the wording of the takbir, which is a pillar of prayer.
The author refers to previous discussion for further detail.
3
Recall the basis
The takbir is a foundational pillar; any intentional alteration that changes the meaning or structure renders the prayer invalid.
This is based on the requirement to pronounce the takbir correctly.
4
Apply the condition
If the hamza is prolonged unintentionally or due to a natural speech impediment, it may not invalidate. However, deliberate prolongation does.
Intent is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفسدها أيضاً مدُّ الهمزة في التكبير، وقدمنـا الكلام عليه، وقراءة ما لا يَحْفَظُهُ مِنْ مصحف، وإن لم يحمله للتلقي من غيره، وأما إذا كان حافظاً له ولم يحمله فلا تفسد لانتفاء العمل والتلقي، (وَ) يفسدها (أداء ركن) كركوع (أو إمكانه) أي: مضي زمن يسع أداء ركن، مع كَشفِ العَوْرَةِ، أو مع نجاسة مانعة لوجود المنافي. أما لو وقع عليه نجاسة فرفعها ولم يبق منها شيء بمجرد وقوعها، أو هبت الريح فكشفته فستر عورته من ساعته فلا يضره
And it [the prayer] is also invalidated by prolonging the hamza in the takbir – and we have previously discussed it – and reading from a mushaf what one does not memorize, even if he does not carry it for receiving from others; but if he has it memorized and does not carry it, then it does not invalidate, due to the absence of action and receipt. And it is invalidated by performing a pillar like bowing, or the possibility of it, meaning the passage of time sufficient to perform a pillar, while the awrah is exposed, or with an impurity that prevents, due to the existence of a contradictory element. But if impurity falls on him and he removes it and nothing of it remains immediately upon its falling, or the wind blows and exposes his awrah, and he covers it immediately, that does not harm him.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage lists three more invalidators of prayer. First, prolonging the hamza in the takbir (e.g., saying "Allaaaah" instead of "Allah") – the author notes this was discussed earlier. Second, reading from a physical mushaf (Qur'an) if the person does not have the passage memorized, because such reading involves action (holding the mushaf) and learning (talaqqi) which are incompatible with prayer. However, if the person has the passage memorized and does not actually carry or handle the mushaf, the prayer is not invalidated. Third, performing any rukn (e.g., ruku') or even the opportunity to perform a rukn while one's awrah is exposed or while there is an impurity that prevents validity, because the presence of a contradictory element (al-manafi) makes the act null. There is an exception: if an impurity falls on the worshipper and he removes it immediately so that no trace remains, or if the wind uncovers his awrah and he covers it immediately, the prayer is not harmed.

Key Terms
مد الهمزة في التكبير (madd al-hamza fi al-takbir): Prolonging the hamza sound when saying Allahu Akbar, changing the meaning or pronunciation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the prayer if a person intentionally prolongs the hamza in the takbir?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid (batil).
C) The prayer is makruh but valid.
D) The prayer requires sajdah sahw.

Key Takeaway
Intentionally prolonging the hamza in the takbir invalidates the prayer because it alters a pillar.

Reading from Mushaf During Prayer: When It Invalidates
Ruling on reciting from a mushaf during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when reading from a mushaf invalidates prayer and distinguish between memorized and unmemorized recitation.

Core Idea
Reading from a mushaf invalidates prayer only if the passage is not memorized and the mushaf is handled for learning.

This lesson addresses the ruling on reading directly from a physical copy of the Qur'an (mushaf) during prayer. The key distinction is whether the reciter has the passage memorized and whether he physically handles the mushaf. Understanding this distinction helps maintain the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine if the person is reading from a mushaf (physical book) what they do not have memorized.
If they have it memorized and do not handle the mushaf, there is no issue.
2
Assess the conditions
The ruling depends on: (a) memorization of the recited portion, (b) whether the mushaf is carried or physically handled.
If unmemorized and handled, the prayer is invalid.
3
Apply the reasoning (ta'lil)
Reading from a mushaf involves action (carrying/turning pages) and talaqqi (learning/receiving), which are incompatible with the state of prayer.
If memorized and not handled, there is no extra action or learning, so prayer remains valid.
4
Note the exception
If the person has the passage memorized but still reads from the mushaf without handling it (e.g., someone holds it for them), does it invalidate? The text does not clearly cover this, but the principle of 'action and receipt' suggests it may still be problematic if it involves receipt.
The safest view is to avoid any reliance on the mushaf during prayer.

Source Text

And it [the prayer] is also invalidated by prolonging the hamza in the takbir – and we have previously discussed it – and reading from a mushaf what one does not memorize, even if he does not carry it for receiving from others; but if he has it memorized and does not carry it, then it does not invalidate, due to the absence of action and receipt. This passage lists three more invalidators of prayer. First, prolonging the hamza in the takbir (e.g., saying "Allaaaah" instead of "Allah") – the author notes this was discussed earlier. Second, reading from a physical mushaf (Qur'an) if the person does not have the passage memorized, because such reading involves action (holding the mushaf) and learning (talaqqi) which are incompatible with prayer. Key Terms

Performing a Pillar with Awrah Exposed or Impurity
Ruling on exposure and impurity during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that performing a pillar (like ruku') while the awrah is exposed or with a preventing impurity invalidates the prayer, and explain the exception for immediate removal.

Core Idea
Performing any pillar while the awrah is uncovered or with impurity invalidates prayer unless the cause is removed instantly.

This lesson deals with the third nullifier: performing a pillar (such as bowing) or merely having the opportunity to perform a pillar while the awrah is exposed or while there is an impurity that prevents validity. The author also provides an important exception for immediate removal of impurity or covering of the awrah. Understanding this helps preserve the validity of prayer in unforeseen circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The nullifier occurs when a pillar (e.g., ruku') is performed, or when time passes sufficient to perform a pillar, while either (a) the awrah is uncovered, or (b) a preventing impurity is present.
The awrah must be covered from the start; impurity must be of a type that is not excused.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
The presence of a contradictory element (al-manafi) – exposure or impurity – during a pillar makes the prayer invalid because the conditions for validity are not met.
A preventing impurity is one that, by its quantity or type, is not exempted.
3
Apply the exception
If impurity falls on the worshipper and he removes it immediately, leaving no trace, the prayer is not harmed. Similarly, if the wind reveals the awrah and he covers it instantly, the prayer remains valid.
The key is immediacy: no significant delay or additional action.
4
Distinguish from other cases
If the impurity remains or the awrah stays uncovered for any length of time that would allow a pillar, the prayer is invalid even if later corrected.
The exception only applies to instantaneous events.

Source Text

And it [the prayer] is also invalidated by prolonging the hamza in the takbir – and we have previously discussed it – and reading from a mushaf what one does not memorize, even if he does not carry it for receiving from others; but if he has it memorized and does not carry it, then it does not invalidate, due to the absence of action and receipt. Key Terms

Key Takeaway

Muqtadi Racing Ahead of Imam in a Rukn
Ruling on a muqtadi who performs a rukn before the imam without the imam joining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the five scenarios of a muqtadi racing ahead in a rukn and state the resulting ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
A muqtadi's prayer is invalid if he races ahead without correction; otherwise, he makes up 1, 2, or 4 rak'ahs depending on timing.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah outlines the rulings for a follower who performs a pillar (ruku' or sujud) before the imam without the imam joining. The Hanafi school details five specific scenarios, each with a distinct consequence ranging from invalidation of the prayer to requiring the follower to make up one, two, or four rak'ahs without recitation. Understanding these scenarios helps the muqtadi maintain the proper sequence of actions in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the overarching principle: the muqtadi must follow the imam in all actions. Racing ahead in a rukn (pillar) without the imam joining invalidates the prayer if not corrected.
Correction means repeating the rukn with the imam or after him.
2
Distinguish invalidation from qada' scenarios
Determine whether the muqtadi says salam with the imam after the mistake. If yes, prayer is batil (invalid). If no, he becomes a lahiq (one who missed a rak'ah) and must make up missed rak'ahs (qada') without recitation.
The lahiq makes up rak'ahs after the imam's salam, and his qada' has no recitation because he is considered to have already recited when following the imam.
3
Analyze the three qada' scenarios
Examine the timing of the muqtadi's bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) relative to the imam. The passage details three patterns: (a) bows and prostrates before imam in all rak'ahs → qada' 1 rak'ah; (b) bows with imam but prostrates before him → qada' 2 rak'ahs; (c) bows before imam but prostrates with him → qada' 4 rak'ahs.
The reasoning involves attaching actions to previous/following rak'ahs based on which rak'ah's pillars were correctly performed.
4
Identify the valid scenario
Note the one scenario where the prayer is completely valid: the muqtadi bows and prostrates after the imam has completed his bowing and prostration. This is the normal, correct following.
This scenario reinforces the principle that the muqtadi must follow, not precede.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يفسدها (مُسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه إمامه)، كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام ولم يعده معه أو بعده، وسلم مع الإمام، أما إذا لم يسلم مع الإمام، وقد أتـي بالركوع والسجود قبله في كل الركعات، فإنه يلزمه قضاء ركعة بلا قراءة؛ لأن مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لاحق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام، وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع والسجود، فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية، وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة فيقضي بعد سلام الإمام ركعة بغير قراءة؛ لأنه لاحق بإدراكه إمامه في أول الصلاة، وإن ركع مع إمامه وسجد قبله لزمه قضاء ركعتين، لأنه يلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى؛ لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغو ركوعه في الثانية؛ لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول، بلا سجود ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر دون ركوعه في الرابعة، لكونه قبل سجوده فيلتحق بـه سـجوده في رابعة الإمام، فيصير عليه [ الثانية ] والرابعة فيقضيهما، وإن ركع قبل إمامه وسجد معه يقضي أربعاً بــلا قراءة؛ لأن السجود لا يعتد به إذا لم يتقدمه ركوع صحيح، وركوعه في كل الركعات قبل الإمام يبطل سجوده الحاصل معه، وأما إن ركع إمامه وسجد ثم ركع وسجد بعده جازت صلاته، فهذه خمس صور مأخوذة من «فتح القدير » و « الخلاصة».
And it [the prayer] is invalidated by the muqtadi racing ahead in a pillar in which his imam did not accompany him. For example, if he bows and raises his head before the imam and does not repeat it with him or after him, and says salam with the imam. But if he does not say salam with the imam, and he has performed bowing and prostration before him in all rak'ahs, then he must make up one rak'ah without recitation; because the one who catches the first rak'ah of the imam is a lahiq, and he makes up before the imam's completion, and he has missed the first rak'ah by leaving following the imam in bowing and prostration. So his bowing and prostration in the second [rak'ah] makes up for the first, in the third for the second, in the fourth for the third, so he makes up after the imam's salam one rak'ah without recitation; because he is a lahiq by having caught the imam at the beginning of the prayer. And if he bowed with the imam and prostrated before him, he must make up two rak'ahs, because his prostrations in the second are attached to his bowing in the first; because it was considered, and his bowing in the second is void because it occurred after his first bowing without prostration. Then his bowing in the third with the imam is considered, but not his bowing in the fourth because it was before his prostration, so his prostration in the fourth of the imam attaches to it, so the second and fourth remain upon him, so he makes them up. And if he bowed before his imam and prostrated with him, he makes up four without recitation; because prostration is not considered if correct bowing does not precede it, and his bowing in all rak'ahs before the imam invalidates his prostrations that occurred with him. But if the imam bowed and prostrated, then he [the muqtadi] bowed and prostrated after him, his prayer is valid. These are five scenarios taken from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage details the ruling on a muqtadi who performs a rukn (like ruku' or sujud) ahead of the imam, without the imam joining him in that rukn. The basic ruling: the prayer is invalidated if he does not repeat the rukn with the imam or after him. However, there are multiple scenarios depending on when he performs the rukn relative to the imam and whether he repeats it. The passage outlines five cases: (1) If he bows, raises his head before the imam, does not repeat, and says salam with the imam, prayer invalid. (2) If he does not say salam with the imam and performed bowing and prostration before him in all rak'ahs (as a lahiq – one who catches the imam from the start of the prayer but then separates), he must make up one rak'ah without recitation after the imam's salam. (3) If he bowed with the imam but prostrated before him, he must make up two rak'ahs. (4) If he bowed before the imam and prostrated with him, he makes up four rak'ahs. (5) If he bows and prostrates after the imam's bowing and prostration, his prayer is valid. These scenarios are derived from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah.

Key Terms
مسابقة المقتدي (musabaqat al-muqtadi): The muqtadi performing a rukn before the imam without the imam's participation.
لاحق (lahiq): A muqtadi who catches the imam from the beginning of the prayer but then misses a rak'ah due to something like sleeping, or as here due to racing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a muqtadi bows with the imam but prostrates before him, how many rak'ahs must he make up?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
A muqtadi must never precede the imam; if he does, the prayer is either invalid or requires making up rak'ahs without recitation depending on his subsequent actions.

Masbuq Following Imam in Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq following sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a masbuq following the imam in sujud al-sahw, distinguishing between cases where his prayer is invalid and where it is valid, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The masbuq's prayer invalidates if he knowingly follows after separation, but the later fatwa validates it if he was unaware.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a nuanced situation: a masbuq (latecomer) who has separated from the imam to complete his own prayer subsequently follows the imam in sujud al-sahw. The classical Hanafi ruling held that such following invalidates the prayer because the masbuq is obligated to be independent. However, later Hanafi scholars refined this, distinguishing between knowledge and ignorance, and the relied-upon fatwa is that the prayer is valid. We will unpack the reasoning and the evolution of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
What is the masbuq doing? Following the imam in sujud al-sahw after having separated (e.g., stood up after imam's salam or after sitting for tashahhud). The issue is whether this following invalidates his prayer.
2
State the initial ruling and its reasoning
According to the matn (Nur al-Idah), the prayer is invalidated because the masbuq re-joins after being obligated to be independent. This is like a new following that invalidates.
The reasoning is based on the concept of infirad (independence); the masbuq must not follow after separation.
3
Identify the exception for following before prostration
If the masbuq has stood and bowed but not yet prostrated, and then the imam prostrates for sahw, the masbuq must follow the imam in that prostration. If he does not follow and continues his own prayer, his prayer is valid because following in a wajib is wajib, but leaving a wajib does not invalidate.
This shows that following in sujud al-sahw is not always prohibited; it depends on timing.
4
Examine the later fatwa and its conditions
Later scholars (al-muta'akhkhirin) ruled that the prayer is valid (ja'izah) generally, and that is the fatwa. Al-Fatawa al-Kubra distinguished based on knowledge: if the masbuq did not know the imam had no sahw, the prayer is not invalidated.
The authority weight shifts from the initial ruling to the later fatwa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is that the prayer is valid, especially if the masbuq was unaware of the imam's sahw. This is the position relied upon for fatwa today.
The tarjih is based on the consensus of later masters and the principle of ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفسدها (متابعة الإمام في سجود السهو للمسبوق) إذا تأكد انفراده بأن قام بعد سلام الإمام أو قبله بعد قعوده قدر التشهد، وقيد ركعته بسجدة فتذكر الإمام سجود سهو فتابعه فسدت صلاته، لأنه اقتدى بغيره بعد وجود الانفراد ووجوبه، فتفسد صلاته، أما لو قام وركع، فقبل سجوده سجد الإمام لسهوه، وجب متابعته الإمام في سجوده ورفض قيامه و قراءته وركوعه فإن لم يعد إلى متابعة الإمام ومضى على قضائه جازت صلاته؛ لأن عود الإمام إلى سجود السهو لا يرفع القعود والباقي على الإمام سجود السهو وهو واجب والمتابعة في الواجب واجبة، وترك الواجب لا يوجب فساد الصلاة، ألا ترى أنه لو تركه الإمام لا تفسد صلاته، فكذا المسبوق ويسجد للسهو بعد الفراغ من قضائه استحساناً، وقيدنا قيام المسبوق بكونه بعد قعود الإمام قدر التشهد؛ لأنه إن كان قبله لم يجز لأن الإمام بقي عليه فرض لا ينفرد بـه المسبوق عنه فتفسد صلاته، وتتصور المسألة أيضاً بما إذا تابع المسبوق إمامه في سجود السهو ثــم تبين، يعني: للمسبوق أنه لم يكن على الإمام سهو، حيث تفسد صلاة المسبوق بمتابعة الإمام؛ للاقتداء في موضع كان عليه الانفراد في ذلك الموضع لا لذات السجدتين، ومن الفقهاء من قال: لا تفسد صلاته بخلاف اللاحق، لأنه مقتد في جميع ما يؤدي فلا تفسد صلاته، كذا في «البدائع » انتهى. وفي « الحاوي»: الأحوط أن المسبوق يعيد صلاته، وفي ( الغياثية»: صلاته أي: المسبوق جائزة عند المتأخرين، وعليه الفتوى انتهى. وقد فصل في « الفتاوى الكبرى» أيضاً بين علمه بسهو إمامه وعدمه، فقال: إن لم يعلم المسبوق أن الإمام لم يكن عليه سجود السهو لم تفسد صلاته، وهو
And it [the prayer] is invalidated by the masbuq following the imam in sujud al-sahw, when his separation is confirmed, by him standing after the imam's salam or before it after his sitting for the extent of the tashahhud, and he ties his rak'ah with one prostration, then the imam remembers a sahw and prostrates, so he follows him, then his prayer is invalidated, because he followed another after the existence of separation and its obligation, so his prayer is invalidated. But if he stood and bowed, then before his prostration the imam prostrated for his sahw, he must follow the imam in his prostration and abandon his standing, recitation, and bowing. If he does not return to following the imam and continues with his qada', his prayer is valid; because the imam's returning to sujud al-sahw does not lift the sitting, and what remains upon the imam is sujud al-sahw, which is wajib, and following in a wajib is wajib. Leaving a wajib does not necessitate invalidation of prayer. Do you not see that if the imam leaves it, his prayer is not invalidated? So too the masbuq, and he prostrates for sahw after finishing his qada' by istihsan. And we restricted the masbuq's standing to being after the imam's sitting for the extent of the tashahhud; because if it is before, it is not permissible because the imam still has a fard upon him that the masbuq cannot perform alone, and it invalidates his prayer. And the issue is also imagined when the masbuq follows his imam in sujud al-sahw and then it becomes clear to the masbuq that the imam did not have sahw, then the masbuq's prayer is invalidated due to following in a place where separation was upon him, not due to the prostration itself. Among the jurists, some said: his prayer is not invalidated, unlike the lahiq, because he is a follower in all that he performs, so his prayer is not invalidated, as in al-Bada'i'. In al-Hawi: the precaution is that the masbuq repeats his prayer. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: his prayer (i.e., the masbuq's) is valid according to the later scholars, and upon that is the fatwa. And in al-Fatawa al-Kubra, it differentiated based on his knowledge of the imam's sahw or lack thereof, saying: if the masbuq did not know that the imam did not have sujud al-sahw, his prayer is not invalidated...
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a masbuq (one who joined the prayer late) follows the imam in sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) after he has separated from the imam. The basic ruling: if the masbuq has clearly separated (e.g., stood up after the imam's salam or after sitting for tashahhud) and then follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, his prayer is invalid because he is re-joining the prayer after having been obligated to be independent. However, there are nuances. If the masbuq has stood and bowed but not yet prostrated, and then the imam prostrates for sahw, the masbuq must follow the imam in that prostration, abandoning his own standing, recitation, and bowing. If he does not follow and continues his own qada', his prayer is valid because following in a wajib (sujud al-sahw is wajib for the imam) is wajib, but leaving it does not invalidate. The masbuq then performs sujud al-sahw after his qada' by istihsan. A key condition: the masbuq's standing must be after the imam's sitting for tashahhud; otherwise, the prayer invalidates. The passage also addresses a case where the masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw and then discovers the imam actually had no sahw. In that case, the prayer invalidates because the masbuq followed in a position where he should have been independent. There is a dispute among later Hanafi scholars: some say the prayer is invalid, others (like in al-Ghiyathiyyah) say it is valid and that is the fatwa. Al-Fatawa al-Kubra distinguishes: if the masbuq did not know the imam had no sahw, the prayer is valid. The passage ends mid-sentence in the OCR.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the prayer late, missing one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
انفراد (infirad): The state of the masbuq being independent from the imam after the imam has completed the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later fatwa (al-muta'akhkhirin) mentioned in the passage, what is the ruling on a masbuq who follows the imam in sujud al-sahw after separating and then discovers the imam had no sahw?
A) His prayer is invalid.
B) His prayer is valid.
C) He must repeat his prayer.
D) He must repeat the prostration.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi ruling is that a masbuq who follows the imam in sujud al-sahw after separation does not invalidate his prayer, especially if he was unaware.

Five Scenarios of Masbuq Following in Sujud al-Sahw
Explaining five scenarios of a masbuq following imam in sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five scenarios of a masbuq following the imam in sujud al-sahw and determine the number of rak'ahs to make up in each.

Core Idea
A masbuq's prayer validity depends on the timing of his bowing and prostrating relative to the imam's sujud al-sahw.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah details five distinct scenarios concerning a latecomer (masbuq) who follows the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw). Depending on when the masbuq bows and prostrates relative to the imam, he may need to make up one, two, or four rak'ahs, or his prayer may be valid without any qada. Understanding these scenarios is essential for correctly completing the prayer when joining late.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five scenarios
Read the passage and list each distinct case described. The passage presents five scenarios, each with a different outcome in terms of how many rak'ahs the masbuq must make up.
The scenarios are demarcated by 'If he bowed...', 'If he bowed before...', etc.
2
Analyze the underlying principle
For each scenario, understand why the number of rak'ahs to make up differs. The key principle is that prostration (sajdah) must be preceded by a valid bowing (ruku'). If the masbuq's sajdah occurs without a valid ruku', that rakat is void.
The lahiq concept: one who caught the imam from the beginning of prayer may have different counting.
3
Apply to case one: lahiq scenario
In the first scenario, the masbuq bows and prostrates with the imam in the second, third, and fourth rak'ahs. Since he caught the imam at the start (lahiq), his recitation is considered, and he makes up only the first rak'ah after the imam's salam.
This is the simplest case.
4
Examine the second and third scenarios
Scenario 2: He bows with imam but prostrates before him → his second rak'ah's sajdah attaches to first rak'ah's ruku', voiding the second ruku', so he makes up two rak'ahs. Scenario 3: He bows before imam and prostrates with him → all his prostrations are invalid, so he makes up four rak'ahs.
The timing of sajdah relative to ruku' is critical.
5
Check the valid scenario and conclude
Scenario 4: He bows and prostrates after the imam (in correct sequence) → his prayer is valid. Scenario 5 is implied: the case where his bowing in the fourth occurs before his prostration leads to needing to make up two rak'ahs (the second and fourth). Verify this from the text.
The overall lesson is that the masbuq must ensure his sajdah follows a valid ruku' from his own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومتابعة الإمام في سجودِ السهو للمسبوق، . عن والسجود، فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية، وفي الرابعة الثالثة فيقضي بعد سلام الإمام ركعة بغير قراءة؛ لأنه لاحق بإدراكه إمامه في أول الصلاة، وإن ركع مع إمامه وسجد قبله لزمه قضاء ركعتين، لأنه يلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى؛ لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغو ركوعه في الثانية؛ لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول، بلا سجود ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر دون ركوعه في الرابعة، لكونه قبل سجوده فيلتحق بـه سـجوده في رابعة الإمام، فيصير عليه [ الثانية ] والرابعة فيقضيهما، وإن ركع قبل إمامه وسجد معه يقضي أربعاً بــلا قراءة؛ لأن السجود لا يعتد به إذا لم يتقدمه ركوع صحيح، وركوعه في كل الركعات قبل الإمام يبطل سجوده الحاصل معه، وأما إن ركع إمامه وسجد ثم ركع وسجد بعده جازت صلاته، فهذه خمس صور مأخوذة من «فتح القدير » و « الخلاصة».
And following the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness for the latecomer. And the prostration: so his bowing and prostration in the second [rak'ah] make up for the first, and in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third, so he prays after the imam's salam one rak'ah without recitation; because he is a lahiq by having caught the imam at the beginning of the prayer. If he bowed with his imam and prostrated before him, he must make up two rak'ahs, because his two prostrations in the second become attached to his bowing in the first (since it was valid), and his bowing in the second is void because it occurred immediately after his first bowing without prostration. Then his bowing in the third with the imam is valid, but not his bowing in the fourth because it occurred before his prostration, so his prostration in the imam's fourth attaches to it, thus the second and fourth become due on him, and he makes them up. If he bowed before his imam and prostrated with him, he makes up four without recitation, because prostration is not valid if not preceded by a valid bowing, and his bowing in all rak'ahs before the imam invalidates his prostration done with him. As for if he bowed when his imam bowed and prostrated, then bowed and prostrated after him, his prayer is valid. These are five scenarios taken from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah.

Commentary
This passage presents five detailed scenarios concerning a masbuq (latecomer) who follows the imam's sujud al-sahw. The ruling: depending on the sequence of rak'ahs and sajdahs, the masbuq may need to make up one, two, or four rak'ahs without recitation. The key principle is that the masbuq's action is evaluated based on how his rak'ahs align with the imam's. The five scenarios are: (1) He bows and prostrates with imam in all except first rak'ah→ make up one rak'ah. (2) He bows with imam but prostrates before him→ make up two. (3) He bows before imam and prostrates with him→ make up four. (4) He bows and prostrates after imam→ prayer valid. (5) The case where his bowing in fourth is before his prostration. The author references Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah as sources.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has already begun the prayer.
لاحق (lahiq): One who catches the imam at the beginning of the prayer but misses some rak'ahs due to a valid excuse.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Takeaway
A masbuq must ensure his sajdah follows a valid ruku' from his own prayer; otherwise, he may need to make up rak'ahs depending on the timing of his actions relative to the imam's sujud al-sahw.

Following the Imam in Sujud al-Sahw After Independence: When It Invalidates
Ruling on invalidation by following imam in sujud al-sahw for masbuq after independence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for invalidation of a masbuq's prayer when following the imam in sujud al-sahw, and distinguish between scenarios where following invalidates versus where it is obligatory.

Core Idea
Following the imam in sujud al-sahw invalidates only after the masbuq's independence (infirad) is established.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a nuanced situation: a masbuq (latecomer) who has reached independence (infirad) must not follow the imam in sujud al-sahw—doing so invalidates his prayer. However, if he has not yet performed his own prostration, he must abandon his actions and follow the imam. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct prayer completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for invalidation
The text states that invalidation occurs when the masbuq's independence is confirmed: he stood after the imam's salam or after the imam sat for tashahhud. Locate this condition in the Arabic.
Independence means he is no longer obliged to follow.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The invalidation is because he followed another after independence had occurred and become obligatory. This shows that following is prohibited once he is on his own.
The proof is aqli (rational) rather than direct text.
3
Contrast with the exception
If the masbuq has bowed but not yet prostrated, and the imam remembers sujud al-sahw, the masbuq must follow the imam. Here, his independence is not yet complete because he hasn't prostrated.
The key is whether he has tied his rak'ah with a prostration.
4
Analyze the consequence of not following in the exception
If the masbuq does not follow and continues on his own, his prayer is still valid because leaving a wajib does not invalidate.
This is contrasted with the invalidation in the first scenario.

(و) يفسدها (متابعة الإمام في سجود السهو للمسبوق) إذا تأكد انفراده بأن قام بعد سلام الإمام أو قبله بعد قعوده قدر التشهد، وقيد ركعته بسجدة فتذكر الإمام سجود سهو فتابعه فسدت صلاته، لأنه اقتدى بغيره بعـد وجـود الانفراد ووجوبه، فتفسد صلاته، أما لو قام وركع، فقبل سجوده سجد الإمام لسهوه، وجب متابعته الإمام في سجوده ورفض قيامه و قراءته وركوعه فإن لم يعد إلى متابعة الإمام ومضى على قضائه جازت صلاته؛ لأن عود الإمام إلى سجود السهو لا يرفع القعود والباقي على الإمام سجود السهو وهو واجب والمتابعة في الواجب واجبة، وترك الواجب لا يوجب فساد الصلاة، ألا ترى أنه لو تركه الإمام لا تفسد صلاته، فكذا المسبوق ويسجد للسهو بعد الفراغ من : قضائه استحساناً، وقيدنا قيام المسبوق بكونه بعد قعود الإمام قدر التشهد؛ لأنه إن كان قبله لم يجز لأن الإمام بقي عليه فرض لا ينفرد بـه المسبوق عنه فتفسد صلاته، وتتصور المسألة أيضاً بما إذا تابع المسبوق إمامه في سجود السهو ثــم تبين، يعني: للمسبوق أنه لم يكن على الإمام سهو، حيث تفسد صلاة المسبوق بمتابعة الإمام؛ للاقتداء في موضع كان عليه الانفراد في ذلك الموضع لا لذات السجدتين، ومن الفقهاء من قال: لا تفسد صلاته بخلاف اللاحق، لأنه مقتد في جميع ما يؤدي فلا تفسد صلاته، كذا في «البدائع » انتهى. وفي « الحاوي»: الأحوط أن المسبوق يعيد صلاته، وفي ( الغياثية»: صلاته أي: المسبوق جائزة عند المتأخرين، وعليه الفتوى انتهى. وقد فصل في « الفتاوى الكبرى» أيضاً بين علمه بسهو إمامه وعدمه، فقال: إن لم يعلم المسبوق أن الإمام لم يكن عليه سجود السهو لم تفسد صلاته، وهـو المختار انتهى. ومثله في ( التجنيس والمزيد » انتهى. وفي ( الخانية»: إن علم تفسد في أشهر الروايتين، كذا في « التاتارخانية». وقد قال «قاضي خان : وإن لم يعلم أي: المسبوق أنه لم يكن على الإمام سهو لم تفسد صلاة المسبوق في قولهم انتهى، وهذا بخلاف ما يفيد الخلاف في حالة عدم علمه في كلام غيره، كما قدمناه انتهى
(And) it (the prayer) is invalidated by (following the imam in sujud al-sahw for the masbuq) when his independence is confirmed, by his standing after the imam's salam or before it after the imam's sitting for the amount of tashahhud, and he ties his rak'ah with a prostration, then the imam remembers sujud al-sahw and the masbuq follows him, his prayer is invalidated. Because he followed another after independence had occurred and become obligatory, so his prayer is invalidated. But if he stood and bowed, then before his prostration the imam prostrated for his forgetfulness, it is obligatory for him to follow the imam in his prostration and abandon his standing, recitation, and bowing. If he does not return to following the imam and continues with his make-up, his prayer is valid. Because the imam's return to sujud al-sahw does not lift the sitting; all that remains on the imam is sujud al-sahw, and it is wajib, and following in the obligatory is obligatory, and leaving the obligatory does not necessitate invalidation of prayer. Do you not see that if the imam leaves it, his prayer is not invalidated? Similarly the masbuq, and he prostrates for forgetfulness after completing his make-up, by istihsan. And we restricted the masbuq's standing to after the imam's sitting for the amount of tashahhud, because if it was before, it is not permissible because a fard remains on the imam which the masbuq cannot perform alone, so his prayer is invalidated. The issue can also be conceived as when the masbuq follows his imam in sujud al-sahw and then it becomes clear to him that the imam had no forgetfulness, where the masbuq's prayer is invalidated by following the imam, because of following in a place where he was required to be independent, not for the prostrations themselves. Some jurists said: his prayer is not invalidated, unlike the lahiq, because he is being led in all that he performs, so his prayer is not invalidated. Thus in al-Bada'i, end. In al-Hawi: the precaution is that the masbuq repeats his prayer. In al-Ghiyathiyyah: his prayer (i.e., the masbuq's) is valid according to the later scholars, and upon it is the fatwa, end. And it is detailed in al-Fatawa al-Kubra also between his knowledge of the imam's forgetfulness and ignorance: if the masbuq did not know that the imam had no sujud al-sahw, his prayer is not invalidated, and that is the chosen opinion, end. Similar is in al-Tajnisi wa al-Mazid, end. In al-Khaniyyah: if he knows, it is invalidated in the more famous of the two narrations. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And Qadi Khan said: if he did not know (i.e., the masbuq) that there was no forgetfulness on the imam, the masbuq's prayer is not invalidated according to their statement, end. And this is contrary to what the difference of opinion in the case of his ignorance in the words of others implies, as we have mentioned, end.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage discusses when following the imam in sujud al-sahw invalidates the masbuq's prayer. The key condition is that the masbuq has already become independent (infirad) after the imam's sitting for tashahhud. If he then follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, his prayer is invalid because he is following after being obliged to be independent. However, if he had already bowed but not prostrated, then he must abandon his own actions and follow. The text presents multiple opinions: al-Bada'i says it is invalidated; al-Hawi recommends repeating; al-Ghiyathiyyah says it is valid according to later scholars. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that if the masbuq was unaware of the imam's forgetfulness, his prayer is not invalidated; if aware, it is invalidated in the more famous narration. The passage illustrates the Hanafi method of weighing different sources and the concept of istihsan.

Key Terms
الانفراد (al-infirad): The state of the masbuq becoming independent from the imam after he has sat for the tashahhud and the masbuq has completed his own standing.
لاحق (lahiq): One who caught the imam from the beginning but missed some rak'ahs due to a valid excuse and remains in the imam's following for the remainder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw after his independence is confirmed?
A) His prayer is valid
B) His prayer is invalid
C) He must repeat the prayer but it is valid
D) He must perform sujud al-sahw only

Key Takeaway
Following the imam in sujud al-sahw after independence invalidates the masbuq's prayer; the exception is when he has not yet prostrated.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Relied-Upon Fatwa on the Masbuq's Following in Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation when masbuq follows imam in sujud al-sahw and later learns the imam had no forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position regarding the masbuq's following of the imam in sujud al-sahw when ignorant of the imam's forgetfulness, and identify the different views within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi is that the masbuq's prayer is valid if he was unaware of the imam's forgetfulness; the more famous narration says it invalidates if he knows.

This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the masbuq's prayer is invalidated when he follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, especially when it later becomes clear the imam had no forgetfulness. Later scholars, including Qadi Khan, preferred the view that ignorance prevents invalidation, which is the operative fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, then discovers the imam had no forgetfulness. Does his prayer invalidate?
The text presents this as a separate case from the initial one.
2
List the different Hanafi opinions
Al-Bada'i says invalid; al-Hawi recommends repeating; al-Ghiyathiyyah says valid; al-Fatawa al-Kubra distinguishes based on knowledge.
Each authority has a different weight.
3
Apply the tarjih (preference)
Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) and Qadi Khan favor the view that if the masbuq was ignorant, his prayer is valid. The more famous narration for the knowing case is invalidation.
The mufta bihi is the differentiated view.
4
Understand the rationale for the lahiq exception
The lahiq is always considered a follower, so his following never invalidates. The masbuq's case is different because he becomes independent.
This highlights the importance of the concept of infirad.
