Chapter on the Disliked Acts of Prayer
Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person: deliberately leaving an obligatory or sunnah act.
Chapter on the Disliked Acts of Prayer
(2) The disliked (makruh) is the opposite of beloved; its definition is that leaving it is better than doing it and seeking it, as was said. This is apparent for the disliked as a matter of tanzih. It is called makruh by virtue of adjacency, like the prohibition of praying on someone else's land. The makruh in this section are two types: one is disliked tanzihan (lightly), and the second is disliked tahriman (prohibitively). When the disliked is mentioned, one must look at its evidence. If it is a zanni (speculative) prohibition, it is ruled as makruh tahrimi, unless there is a factor diverting the prohibition from tahrim to nadb. If the evidence is not a prohibition but rather indicates non-committal abandonment, it is tanzihi. It was said: if it entails leaving an obligatory act, it is makruh tahrimi; if it entails leaving a sunnah, it is makruh tanzihi. End. Makruh tahrimi is closer to haram, and makruh tanzihi is closer to halal. The prayer is valid in all forms of karahah because its conditions are fulfilled, and it is repeated in a non-disliked manner. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah. It is stated in al-Tajnīs wal-Mazīd: Every prayer performed with karahah shall be repeated in a non-disliked manner. And his statement, peace be upon him: 'No prayer similar to it should be prayed after it' is interpreted as prohibiting repetition due to waswasa (whisperings), so it does not include repetition due to karahah. This was mentioned by Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in al-Jami' al-Saghir. End. This includes repetition for makruh tanzih. The example of Shaykh Akmal al-Din regarding the obligatory (in his statement: 'and it is repeated in a non-disliked manner, meaning the prayer is repeated out of precaution in a manner that has no karahah, and this is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah, just as if one left an obligatory act of prayer') does not prevent it, because repetition for leaving an obligatory act is obligatory, so it does not prevent that repetition may be recommended for leaving a sunnah, since karahah exists by leaving the sunnah, and the indefinite in the context of negation—by his saying: 'repeated in a manner that has no karahah'—generically includes makruh tanzih and tahrim. (Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person, approximately not exactly: deliberately leaving an obligatory or sunnah act. He began with this because what follows is like a command.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah begins the chapter on the disliked acts (makruhat) of prayer. The passage type is a definition_ruling, as it defines the term 'makruh' and establishes the ruling for prayers performed with karahah. The author explains that makruh (disliked) is of two types: makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) and makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The distinction is based on the strength of the evidence: a zanni (speculative) prohibition indicates karahah tahrimi, while evidence suggesting mere avoidance without emphasis indicates karahah tanzihi. Alternatively, leaving a wajib act results in karahah tahrimi, and leaving a sunnah results in karahah tanzihi. The key ruling is that any prayer performed with makruh (whether tanzih or tahrimi) is valid because its essential conditions are met, but it should be repeated (i'adah) in a non-disliked manner as a precaution. This repetition is either wajib (if a wajib was left) or mandub (if a sunnah was left). The author cites al-Tajnīs wal-Mazīd and al-Bazdawi to support this, and interprets a hadith 'No prayer similar to it should be prayed after it' as referring to waswasa, not repetition due to karahah. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is comprehensive: repetition is called for even for makruh tanzih, as the general wording 'on a manner that has no karahah' includes both types.

Key Terms
مكروه تحريماً (makruh tahriman): A disliked act that is prohibitively so, meaning it is close to haram; leaving a wajib results in this.
مكروه تنزيهاً (makruh tanzihan): A lightly disliked act; leaving a sunnah results in this; leaving it is better than doing it.
إعادة (i'adah): Repeating the prayer after it has been performed; required when the prayer had karahah, either wajib (if a wajib was omitted) or mandub (if a sunnah was omitted).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person deliberately leaves a sunnah act in prayer, what type of karahah does this entail?
A) Makruh tahrimi
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Prayer with any karahah is valid but must be repeated; the type of makruh determines whether repetition is wajib or mandub.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Definition and Classification of Makruh in Prayer
Defines makruh and classifies its two levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of makruh and distinguish between makruh tanzihi and makruh tahrimi based on the evidence.

Core Idea
Makruh is of two types: tahrimi (closer to haram) and tanzihi (closer to halal); the distinction depends on evidence strength.

This lesson unpacks the core Hanafi definition of makruh in prayer. Not all disliked acts are equal: some are prohibitively disliked due to a speculative prohibition, others lightly disliked. Understanding this classification is crucial for determining the weight of an action and whether repetition is recommended or obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of makruh
Read the text's definition: 'that whose abandonment is better than its doing.' Note that this applies to tanzihi.
The definition is qualified as 'apparent in makruh tanzihi'.
2
Distinguish the two types
The text explicitly divides makruh into tanzihi and tahrimi. Recognize that tahrimi is based on a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni).
Unless a factor turns the prohibition to recommendation.
3
Understand the criteria for each type
If the evidence includes a nahy zanni, it is tahrimi; if not, or if it merely indicates preferred abandonment, it is tanzihi. Also, omission of a wajib leads to tahrimi, omission of a sunnah leads to tanzihi.
These criteria may overlap.
4
Relate to proximity
Tahrimi is closer to haram, tanzihi closer to halal. This helps assess the gravity of the act.

(يُكْرَه للمُصَلِّي سَبْعَةٌ وَسَبْعُونَ شَيْئَاً تقريباً لا تحديداً : تَرْكُ واجب، أو سنّةٍ عَمْداً صدر بهذا لأنه لما بعده كالأمر الكلي المنطبق على جزئيات كثيرة، كـ ترك الاطمئنان في الأركان، وكـ مسابقة الإمام، لما فيها من الوعيد على ما في الصحيحين: « أمَا يَخْشَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ رَأْسَهُ رَأْسَ حِمَارٍ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ صُورَتَهُ صُورَةَ حِمَارٍ » وكمجاوزة اليدين الأذنين، وجعلهما تحت المنكبين، وستر القدمين في السجود عمداً للرجال، (كعبيه بثوبه، وبدنهِ لأن العبث ينافي الخشوع الذي هو روح الصلاة، فكان مكروهاً لقوله تعالى: (قَدْ أَفْلَحَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ ) الَّذِينَ هُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ خَشِعُونَ ( ) الو ] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ الله كَرِهَ لَكُمْ العَبَثَ فِي الصَّلاةِ، وَالرَّفَثَ فِي الصَّيَامِ، والضَحِكَ عِنْدَ المَقَابِرِ » وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «كُفُوا أَيْدِيَكُمْ فِي الصَّلاةِ » ورأى عليه الصلاة والسلام رجلاً يعبث بلحيته في الصَّلاةِ فقال : ( لو خَشَعَ قَلْبُهُ لَخَشَعَتْ جوارحه ) والعبث: عبارة عن عمل لا فائدة فيه، ولا مصلحة ولا حكمة تقتضيه، وقال الإمام بدر الدين الكردري: إنه فعل فيه غرض ليس بشرعي، والسفه ما لا غرض فيه أصلاً. وقال الإمام حميد الدين: العبث كل عمل ليس فيه غرض، وقال الشيخ أكمل الدين ولا نزاع في الاصطلاح، وقال الديـــري: المذكور في شروح الهداية» وغيرها: إن العبث الفعل لغرض غير صحيح، والتحقيق أن المراد بالعبث ها هنا: فعل ما ليس من أفعال الصلاة، لأنه ينافي الصلاة. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ فِي الصَّلاةِ شُغلا » انتهى. وفي مجمع الروايات»: قال في «البدرية ) : : المحرمات أربعة: العبث، والسفه، والجهل، والظلم، ونسبة العبث إلى السفه كنسبة الجهل إلى الظلم. فإن في السفه والظلم إضراراً دون العبث والجهل، فإن فيهما ضرراً لا إضراراً، والسفه أقوى من العبث كالظلم أقوى من الجهل، والعبث: عبارة عن فعل يخلو عن الفائدة، والسفه: عبارة عن ما يوجب المضرة، وفي « الهداية » : العبث خارج الصلاة حرام، فما ظنك به في الصلاة ، وفي ( الحميدي العبث حرام لقولـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام:
Chapter on the Disliked Acts of Prayer. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person: deliberately leaving an obligatory (wajib) or a sunnah act. (2) The disliked (makruh) is the opposite of the beloved (mahbub); it is that whose abandonment is better than its doing and acquisition, as was said. This is apparent in the case of makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). It is called makruh by virtue of adjacency, like the prohibition of praying in someone else's land. The disliked in this chapter are of two types: one is tanzihi, and the second is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). So when the disliked is mentioned, one must consider its evidence. If it is a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni), it is judged as makruh tahrimi, unless there is a factor turning the prohibition from tahrim to nadb. If the evidence is not a prohibition but rather indicates non-commitment to abandonment, then it is tanzihi. It is said: if it involves leaving a wajib, it is makruh tahrimi; if it involves leaving a sunnah, it is makruh tanzihi, end. Makruh tahrimi is closer to prohibition (haram), and makruh tanzihi is closer to permissible (halal). The prayer is valid in all forms of dislike because its conditions are fulfilled, but it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike. It is stated in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd: Every prayer performed with dislike must be repeated without the disliked element. His statement (peace be upon him): 'No prayer after it is like it' is interpreted as a prohibition of repetition due to waswasa (whisperings), so it does not include repetition due to dislike. This was mentioned by Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, end. This includes repetition due to tanzihi dislike, and the example of Shaykh Akmal al-Din regarding wajib does not prevent it. His saying: 'and it is repeated in a non-disliked manner' means the prayer is repeated out of precaution in a manner without dislike. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike, as when one leaves a wajib from the wajibat of prayer, end. Because repetition due to leaving a wajib is obligatory, it does not prevent that repetition could be recommended due to leaving a sunnah; because the disliked exists with leaving sunnah, and the indefinite noun in the context of negation in his saying 'without dislike' encompasses both tanzihi and tahrimi dislike. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person approximately, not definitively: deliberately leaving a wajib or a sunnah. He began with this because it is like a universal principle that applies to many particulars, such as leaving tranquility (itminan) in the pillars, and such as racing the imam, due to the threat in the Two Sahihs: 'Does not one of you fear, when he raises his head before the imam, that Allah will make his head like the head of a donkey, or make his form like the form of a donkey?' And such as passing the hands beyond the ears, and placing them below the shoulders, and covering the feet in prostration deliberately for men, and playing with his garment, his body, because frivolity (ʿabath) contradicts khushuʿ (humility), which is the spirit of prayer. So it is disliked due to His saying: 'Indeed successful are the believers who in their prayer are humble' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah dislikes for you frivolity in prayer, obscenity in fasting, and laughter at graveyards' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Restrain your hands in prayer' and he saw a man playing with his beard in prayer and said: 'Had his heart been humble, his limbs would have been humble.' Al-ʿAbath is an action with no benefit, interest, or wisdom requiring it. Imam Badr al-Din al-Kardari said: It is an action with a purpose that is not legal, while safah (foolishness) is an action with no purpose at all. Imam Hamid al-Din said: Al-ʿAbath is every action with no purpose. Shaykh Akmal al-Din said: There is no dispute in terminology. Al-Dayri said: What is mentioned in the commentaries of al-Hidayah and others: Al-ʿAbath is an action for an invalid purpose. The verification is that the intended meaning of ʿabath here is doing what is not from the actions of prayer, because it contradicts prayer. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed in prayer there is occupation' end. In Majmaʿ al-Riwayat: It is said in al-Badriyya: Prohibited things are four: al-ʿabath, al-safah, al-jahl, and al-zulm. The relation of ʿabath to safah is like the relation of jahl to zulm. For in safah and zulm there is harm (idrar), unlike ʿabath and jahl, for in them there is detriment (darar) without harm. Safah is stronger than ʿabath just as zulm is stronger than jahl. Al-ʿAbath is an action devoid of benefit; al-safah is that which entails harm. In al-Hidayah: Al-ʿAbath outside prayer is haram, so what do you think about it in prayer? And in al-Humaydi: Al-ʿAbath is haram due to his saying (peace be upon him):
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, typical of the Hanafi school. It begins by defining the term 'makruh' and distinguishing its two levels: tanzihi (lightly disliked) and tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). A makruh tanzihi is where abandonment is preferred but the act is not sinful, while makruh tahrimi is closer to haram and requires a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni). The commentary then clarifies that despite the dislike, the prayer remains valid because its essential conditions are met; however, it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner as a precaution. This ruling applies universally to any prayer performed with dislike. The author addresses a potential contradiction with a hadith that might suggest not repeating a prayer, but explains that hadith refers to repetition due to waswasa, not due to dislike. The passage then lists approximately seventy-seven disliked things, beginning with the universal principle that intentionally omitting a wajib or sunnah act is disliked. It provides examples such as lacking tranquility in pillars, racing the imam (citing a strong hadith warning), and various physical actions like passing hands beyond ears or placing them below shoulders. A significant portion is devoted to the concept of 'abath (frivolous action), defined as an action with no legitimate purpose, which contradicts khushu' (humility), the spirit of prayer. The commentary reviews different scholarly definitions, concluding that 'abath in prayer means doing anything not from the acts of prayer. It is deemed disliked or even haram based on hadith and Quranic verses. This analysis is firmly rooted in the Hanafi tradition, with references to key works like al-Hidayah and the rulings of Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action whose abandonment is preferable to its performance; may be tanzihi (lightly disliked) or tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
عبث (ʿabath): An action with no legitimate purpose or benefit; in prayer, any act not from the actions of prayer that contradicts khushuʿ.
خشوع (khushuʿ): Humility and focus in prayer, considered its spirit; its opposite is frivolity (ʿabath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Makruh tahrimi is closer to haram and requires a speculative prohibition; makruh tanzihi is closer to halal and has no prohibition.
B) Makruh tahrimi invalidates the prayer; makruh tanzihi does not.
C) Makruh tahrimi involves omitting a sunnah; makruh tanzihi involves omitting a wajib.
D) There is no practical difference between them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between makruh tanzihi and tahrimi is based on the strength of the evidence and determines whether repetition is recommended or obligatory.

Validity and Repetition of Prayers Performed with Dislike
Ruling on validity and recommended repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that a prayer performed with dislike is valid but should be repeated in a non-disliked manner, and explain the exception for repetition due to waswasa.

Core Idea
A prayer with any disliked element is valid but must be repeated as a precaution, except when repetition is due to waswasa.

This lesson focuses on the practical consequence of performing a prayer with dislike. The text clarifies that despite the validity of the prayer, it should be repeated to avoid the disliked aspect. It also addresses a potential conflict with a hadith that might discourage repetition, explaining the exception for waswasa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on validity
Read that the prayer is valid in all forms of dislike because its conditions are fulfilled.
Validity is not compromised by dislike.
2
Note the requirement to repeat
The text states that the prayer should be repeated in a non-disliked manner. This is a precaution.
Repetition is recommended, not obligatory in all cases? The text says 'tu'ad' (is repeated), but later clarifies it encompasses both tanzihi and tahrimi.
3
Understand the exception
The hadith 'no prayer after it is like it' is interpreted as prohibiting repetition due to waswasa, not due to dislike.
This reconciles the hadith with the recommendation to repeat.

فصل في مكروهات الصلاة
يُكْرَهُ لِلْمُصَلِّي سَبْعَةٌ وَسَبْعُونَ شَيْئاً: تَرْكُ واجب، أو سنة، عمداً.
فصل في مكروهات الصلاة
(۲)
المكروه: ضد المحبوب وحده ما يكون تركه أولى من فعله وتحصيله، كذا قيل، وهذا ظاهر في المكروه تنزيهاً، ويسمى مكروهاً باعتبار المجاور، كالنهي عن الصلاة في أرض الغير، والمكروه في هذا الباب نوعان: أحدهما: ما كره تنزيهاً، والثاني: ما كره تحريماً، فإذا ذكر المكروه لابد من النظر في دليله، فإن كان نهياً ظنياً يحكم بكراهة التحريم، إلا لصارف للنهي عن التحريم إلى الندب، وإن لم يكن الدليل نهياً بل كان مفيداً للترك الغير الجازم، فهي تنزيهية، وقيل: إن تضمن ترك واجب فهو مكروه تحريماً، وإن تضمن ترك سنة فهو مكروه تنزيهاً، انتهى. والمكروه تحريماً إلى الحرمة أقرب، والمكروه تنزيهاً إلى الحل أقرب. فالصلاة صحيحة في جميع صور الكراهة لاستجماع شرائطها، وتعاد على وجه غير مكروه، وهو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة. قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » : وكل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة فإنها تعاد لا على وجه الكراهة. وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « لا يُصَلَّى بَعْدَها صَلاةٌ مثلُها » تأويله: النهي عن الإعادة بسبب الوسوسة، فلا يتناول الإعادة بسبب الكراهية، ذكره صدر الإسلام البزدوي في ( الجامع الصغير»، انتهى. وهذا شامل للإعادة بكراهة التنزيه، ولا يمنع منه تمثيل الشيخ أكمل الدين بالواجب في قوله وتعاد على وجه غير مكروه أي تعاد الصلاة للاحتياط على وجه ليس فيه كراهة، وهو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة، كما إذا ترك واجباً من واجبات الصلاة، انتهى. لأن الإعادة بترك الواجب واجبة، فلا تمنع أن تكون الإعادة مندوبة بترك سنة؛ لأن المكروه موجود بترك السنة، والنكرة في سياق النفي -بقوله: تعاد على وجه ليس فيه كراهة تعم المكروه تنزيهاً وتحريماً. (يُكْرَه للمُصَلِّي سَبْعَةٌ وَسَبْعُونَ شَيْئَاً تقريباً لا تحديداً : تَرْكُ واجب، أو سنّةٍ عَمْداً صدر بهذا لأنه لما بعده كالأمر الكلي المنطبق على جزئيات كثيرة، كـ ترك الاطمئنان في الأركان، وكـ مسابقة الإمام، لما فيها من الوعيد على ما في الصحيحين: « أمَا يَخْشَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ رَأْسَهُ رَأْسَ حِمَارٍ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ صُورَتَهُ صُورَةَ حِمَارٍ » وكمجاوزة اليدين الأذنين، وجعلهما تحت المنكبين، وستر القدمين في السجود عمداً للرجال، (كعبيه بثوبه، وبدنهِ لأن العبث ينافي الخشوع الذي هو روح الصلاة، فكان مكروهاً لقوله تعالى: (قَدْ أَفْلَحَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ ) الَّذِينَ هُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ خَشِعُونَ ( ) الو ] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ الله كَرِهَ لَكُمْ العَبَثَ فِي الصَّلاةِ، وَالرَّفَثَ فِي الصَّيَامِ، والضَحِكَ عِنْدَ المَقَابِرِ » وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «كُفُوا أَيْدِيَكُمْ فِي الصَّلاةِ » ورأى عليه الصلاة والسلام رجلاً يعبث بلحيته في الصَّلاةِ فقال : ( لو خَشَعَ قَلْبُهُ لَخَشَعَتْ جوارحه ) والعبث: عبارة عن عمل لا فائدة فيه، ولا مصلحة ولا حكمة تقتضيه، وقال الإمام بدر الدين الكردري: إنه فعل فيه غرض ليس بشرعي، والسفه ما لا غرض فيه أصلاً. وقال الإمام حميد الدين: العبث كل عمل ليس فيه غرض، وقال الشيخ أكمل الدين ولا نزاع في الاصطلاح، وقال الديـــري: المذكور في شروح الهداية» وغيرها: إن العبث الفعل لغرض غير صحيح، والتحقيق أن المراد بالعبث ها هنا: فعل ما ليس من أفعال الصلاة، لأنه ينافي الصلاة. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ فِي الصَّلاةِ شُغلا » انتهى. وفي مجمع الروايات»: قال في «البدرية ) : : المحرمات أربعة: العبث، والسفه، والجهل، والظلم، ونسبة العبث إلى السفه كنسبة الجهل إلى الظلم. فإن في السفه والظلم إضراراً دون العبث والجهل، فإن فيهما ضرراً لا إضراراً، والسفه أقوى من العبث كالظلم أقوى من الجهل، والعبث: عبارة عن فعل يخلو عن الفائدة، والسفه: عبارة عن ما يوجب المضرة، وفي « الهداية » : العبث خارج الصلاة حرام، فما ظنك به في الصلاة ، وفي ( الحميدي العبث حرام لقولـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام:
Chapter on the Disliked Acts of Prayer. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person: deliberately leaving an obligatory (wajib) or a sunnah act. (2) The disliked (makruh) is the opposite of the beloved (mahbub); it is that whose abandonment is better than its doing and acquisition, as was said. This is apparent in the case of makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). It is called makruh by virtue of adjacency, like the prohibition of praying in someone else's land. The disliked in this chapter are of two types: one is tanzihi, and the second is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). So when the disliked is mentioned, one must consider its evidence. If it is a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni), it is judged as makruh tahrimi, unless there is a factor turning the prohibition from tahrim to nadb. If the evidence is not a prohibition but rather indicates non-commitment to abandonment, then it is tanzihi. It is said: if it involves leaving a wajib, it is makruh tahrimi; if it involves leaving a sunnah, it is makruh tanzihi, end. Makruh tahrimi is closer to prohibition (haram), and makruh tanzihi is closer to permissible (halal). The prayer is valid in all forms of dislike because its conditions are fulfilled, but it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike. It is stated in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd: Every prayer performed with dislike must be repeated without the disliked element. His statement (peace be upon him): 'No prayer after it is like it' is interpreted as a prohibition of repetition due to waswasa (whisperings), so it does not include repetition due to dislike. This was mentioned by Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, end. This includes repetition due to tanzihi dislike, and the example of Shaykh Akmal al-Din regarding wajib does not prevent it. His saying: 'and it is repeated in a non-disliked manner' means the prayer is repeated out of precaution in a manner without dislike. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike, as when one leaves a wajib from the wajibat of prayer, end. Because repetition due to leaving a wajib is obligatory, it does not prevent that repetition could be recommended due to leaving a sunnah; because the disliked exists with leaving sunnah, and the indefinite noun in the context of negation in his saying 'without dislike' encompasses both tanzihi and tahrimi dislike. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person approximately, not definitively: deliberately leaving a wajib or a sunnah. He began with this because it is like a universal principle that applies to many particulars, such as leaving tranquility (itminan) in the pillars, and such as racing the imam, due to the threat in the Two Sahihs: 'Does not one of you fear, when he raises his head before the imam, that Allah will make his head like the head of a donkey, or make his form like the form of a donkey?' And such as passing the hands beyond the ears, and placing them below the shoulders, and covering the feet in prostration deliberately for men, and playing with his garment, his body, because frivolity (ʿabath) contradicts khushuʿ (humility), which is the spirit of prayer. So it is disliked due to His saying: 'Indeed successful are the believers who in their prayer are humble' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah dislikes for you frivolity in prayer, obscenity in fasting, and laughter at graveyards' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Restrain your hands in prayer' and he saw a man playing with his beard in prayer and said: 'Had his heart been humble, his limbs would have been humble.' Al-ʿAbath is an action with no benefit, interest, or wisdom requiring it. Imam Badr al-Din al-Kardari said: It is an action with a purpose that is not legal, while safah (foolishness) is an action with no purpose at all. Imam Hamid al-Din said: Al-ʿAbath is every action with no purpose. Shaykh Akmal al-Din said: There is no dispute in terminology. Al-Dayri said: What is mentioned in the commentaries of al-Hidayah and others: Al-ʿAbath is an action for an invalid purpose. The verification is that the intended meaning of ʿabath here is doing what is not from the actions of prayer, because it contradicts prayer. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed in prayer there is occupation' end. In Majmaʿ al-Riwayat: It is said in al-Badriyya: Prohibited things are four: al-ʿabath, al-safah, al-jahl, and al-zulm. The relation of ʿabath to safah is like the relation of jahl to zulm. For in safah and zulm there is harm (idrar), unlike ʿabath and jahl, for in them there is detriment (darar) without harm. Safah is stronger than ʿabath just as zulm is stronger than jahl. Al-ʿAbath is an action devoid of benefit; al-safah is that which entails harm. In al-Hidayah: Al-ʿAbath outside prayer is haram, so what do you think about it in prayer? And in al-Humaydi: Al-ʿAbath is haram due to his saying (peace be upon him):
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, typical of the Hanafi school. It begins by defining the term 'makruh' and distinguishing its two levels: tanzihi (lightly disliked) and tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). A makruh tanzihi is where abandonment is preferred but the act is not sinful, while makruh tahrimi is closer to haram and requires a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni). The commentary then clarifies that despite the dislike, the prayer remains valid because its essential conditions are met; however, it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner as a precaution. This ruling applies universally to any prayer performed with dislike. The author addresses a potential contradiction with a hadith that might suggest not repeating a prayer, but explains that hadith refers to repetition due to waswasa, not due to dislike. The passage then lists approximately seventy-seven disliked things, beginning with the universal principle that intentionally omitting a wajib or sunnah act is disliked. It provides examples such as lacking tranquility in pillars, racing the imam (citing a strong hadith warning), and various physical actions like passing hands beyond ears or placing them below shoulders. A significant portion is devoted to the concept of 'abath (frivolous action), defined as an action with no legitimate purpose, which contradicts khushu' (humility), the spirit of prayer. The commentary reviews different scholarly definitions, concluding that 'abath in prayer means doing anything not from the acts of prayer. It is deemed disliked or even haram based on hadith and Quranic verses. This analysis is firmly rooted in the Hanafi tradition, with references to key works like al-Hidayah and the rulings of Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action whose abandonment is preferable to its performance; may be tanzihi or tahrimi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a prayer performed with makruh tanzihi?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but it is recommended to repeat it without the disliked element.
D) The prayer is valid but it must be repeated because it is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Every prayer with a disliked element must be repeated as a precaution, except when the repetition is motivated by waswasa.

Examples of Disliked Acts and the Concept of 'Abath
Lists examples of disliked acts and defines 'abath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of disliked acts in prayer and explain why 'abath is considered makruh based on its contradiction with khushu'.

Core Idea
'Abath (frivolity) in prayer is disliked because it destroys khushu', the spirit of prayer.

This lesson explores practical examples of disliked acts, focusing on the concept of 'abath. The text lists about seventy-seven disliked acts, starting with deliberate omission of wajib or sunnah. It then delves into definitions of 'abath and its relation to khushu', concluding that 'abath is any action not from the acts of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the universal principle
The list begins with 'deliberately leaving a wajib or sunnah'. This is the overarching principle that generates many specific examples.
This is an approximative count.
2
Note specific examples
Examples include lacking tranquility in pillars, racing the imam, passing hands beyond ears, placing hands below shoulders, covering feet in prostration, and playing with garment or body.
Each of these contradicts khushu' or involves 'abath.
3
Study 'abath in detail
Read the definitions from various commentators: action with no benefit, no purpose, or an action not from the acts of prayer. The author verifies that 'abath in prayer is doing something not from the actions of prayer.
'Abath outside prayer is haram, inside prayer it is makruh.

(۲)
المكروه: ضد المحبوب وحده ما يكون تركه أولى من فعله وتحصيله، كذا قيل، وهذا ظاهر في المكروه تنزيهاً، ويسمى مكروهاً باعتبار المجاور، كالنهي عن الصلاة في أرض الغير، والمكروه في هذا الباب نوعان: أحدهما: ما كره تنزيهاً، والثاني: ما كره تحريماً، فإذا ذكر المكروه لابد من النظر في دليله، فإن كان نهياً ظنياً يحكم بكراهة التحريم، إلا لصارف للنهي عن التحريم إلى الندب، وإن لم يكن الدليل نهياً بل كان مفيداً للترك الغير الجازم، فهي تنزيهية، وقيل: إن تضمن ترك واجب فهو مكروه تحريماً، وإن تضمن ترك سنة فهو مكروه تنزيهاً، انتهى. والمكروه تحريماً إلى الحرمة أقرب، والمكروه تنزيهاً إلى الحل أقرب. فالصلاة صحيحة في جميع صور الكراهة لاستجماع شرائطها، وتعاد على وجه غير مكروه، وهو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة. قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » : وكل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة فإنها تعاد لا على وجه الكراهة. وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « لا يُصَلَّى بَعْدَها صَلاةٌ مثلُها » تأويله: النهي عن الإعادة بسبب الوسوسة، فلا يتناول الإعادة بسبب الكراهية، ذكره صدر الإسلام البزدوي في ( الجامع الصغير»، انتهى. وهذا شامل للإعادة بكراهة التنزيه، ولا يمنع منه تمثيل الشيخ أكمل الدين بالواجب في قوله وتعاد على وجه غير مكروه أي تعاد الصلاة للاحتياط على وجه ليس فيه كراهة، وهو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة، كما إذا ترك واجباً من واجبات الصلاة، انتهى. لأن الإعادة بترك الواجب واجبة، فلا تمنع أن تكون الإعادة مندوبة بترك سنة؛ لأن المكروه موجود بترك السنة، والنكرة في سياق النفي -بقوله: تعاد على وجه ليس فيه كراهة تعم المكروه تنزيهاً وتحريماً. (يُكْرَه للمُصَلِّي سَبْعَةٌ وَسَبْعُونَ شَيْئَاً تقريباً لا تحديداً : تَرْكُ واجب، أو سنّةٍ عَمْداً صدر بهذا لأنه لما بعده كالأمر الكلي المنطبق على جزئيات كثيرة، كـ ترك الاطمئنان في الأركان، وكـ مسابقة الإمام، لما فيها من الوعيد على ما في الصحيحين: « أمَا يَخْشَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ رَأْسَهُ رَأْسَ حِمَارٍ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ صُورَتَهُ صُورَةَ حِمَارٍ » وكمجاوزة اليدين الأذنين، وجعلهما تحت المنكبين، وستر القدمين في السجود عمداً للرجال، (كعبيه بثوبه، وبدنهِ لأن العبث ينافي الخشوع الذي هو روح الصلاة، فكان مكروهاً لقوله تعالى: (قَدْ أَفْلَحَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ ) الَّذِينَ هُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ خَشِعُونَ ( ) الو ] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ الله كَرِهَ لَكُمْ العَبَثَ فِي الصَّلاةِ، وَالرَّفَثَ فِي الصَّيَامِ، والضَحِكَ عِنْدَ المَقَابِرِ » وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «كُفُوا أَيْدِيَكُمْ فِي الصَّلاةِ » ورأى عليه الصلاة والسلام رجلاً يعبث بلحيته في الصَّلاةِ فقال : ( لو خَشَعَ قَلْبُهُ لَخَشَعَتْ جوارحه ) والعبث: عبارة عن عمل لا فائدة فيه، ولا مصلحة ولا حكمة تقتضيه، وقال الإمام بدر الدين الكردري: إنه فعل فيه غرض ليس بشرعي، والسفه ما لا غرض فيه أصلاً. وقال الإمام حميد الدين: العبث كل عمل ليس فيه غرض، وقال الشيخ أكمل الدين ولا نزاع في الاصطلاح، وقال الديـــري: المذكور في شروح الهداية» وغيرها: إن العبث الفعل لغرض غير صحيح، والتحقيق أن المراد بالعبث ها هنا: فعل ما ليس من أفعال الصلاة، لأنه ينافي الصلاة. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ فِي الصَّلاةِ شُغلا » انتهى. وفي مجمع الروايات»: قال في «البدرية ) : : المحرمات أربعة: العبث، والسفه، والجهل، والظلم، ونسبة العبث إلى السفه كنسبة الجهل إلى الظلم. فإن في السفه والظلم إضراراً دون العبث والجهل، فإن فيهما ضرراً لا إضراراً، والسفه أقوى من العبث كالظلم أقوى من الجهل، والعبث: عبارة عن فعل يخلو عن الفائدة، والسفه: عبارة عن ما يوجب المضرة، وفي « الهداية » : العبث خارج الصلاة حرام، فما ظنك به في الصلاة ، وفي ( الحميدي العبث حرام لقولـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام:
Chapter on the Disliked Acts of Prayer. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person: deliberately leaving an obligatory (wajib) or a sunnah act. (2) The disliked (makruh) is the opposite of the beloved (mahbub); it is that whose abandonment is better than its doing and acquisition, as was said. This is apparent in the case of makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). It is called makruh by virtue of adjacency, like the prohibition of praying in someone else's land. The disliked in this chapter are of two types: one is tanzihi, and the second is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). So when the disliked is mentioned, one must consider its evidence. If it is a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni), it is judged as makruh tahrimi, unless there is a factor turning the prohibition from tahrim to nadb. If the evidence is not a prohibition but rather indicates non-commitment to abandonment, then it is tanzihi. It is said: if it involves leaving a wajib, it is makruh tahrimi; if it involves leaving a sunnah, it is makruh tanzihi, end. Makruh tahrimi is closer to prohibition (haram), and makruh tanzihi is closer to permissible (halal). The prayer is valid in all forms of dislike because its conditions are fulfilled, but it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike. It is stated in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd: Every prayer performed with dislike must be repeated without the disliked element. His statement (peace be upon him): 'No prayer after it is like it' is interpreted as a prohibition of repetition due to waswasa (whisperings), so it does not include repetition due to dislike. This was mentioned by Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, end. This includes repetition due to tanzihi dislike, and the example of Shaykh Akmal al-Din regarding wajib does not prevent it. His saying: 'and it is repeated in a non-disliked manner' means the prayer is repeated out of precaution in a manner without dislike. This is the ruling for every prayer performed with dislike, as when one leaves a wajib from the wajibat of prayer, end. Because repetition due to leaving a wajib is obligatory, it does not prevent that repetition could be recommended due to leaving a sunnah; because the disliked exists with leaving sunnah, and the indefinite noun in the context of negation in his saying 'without dislike' encompasses both tanzihi and tahrimi dislike. Seventy-seven things are disliked for the praying person approximately, not definitively: deliberately leaving a wajib or a sunnah. He began with this because it is like a universal principle that applies to many particulars, such as leaving tranquility (itminan) in the pillars, and such as racing the imam, due to the threat in the Two Sahihs: 'Does not one of you fear, when he raises his head before the imam, that Allah will make his head like the head of a donkey, or make his form like the form of a donkey?' And such as passing the hands beyond the ears, and placing them below the shoulders, and covering the feet in prostration deliberately for men, and playing with his garment, his body, because frivolity (ʿabath) contradicts khushuʿ (humility), which is the spirit of prayer. So it is disliked due to His saying: 'Indeed successful are the believers who in their prayer are humble' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah dislikes for you frivolity in prayer, obscenity in fasting, and laughter at graveyards' and His saying (peace be upon him): 'Restrain your hands in prayer' and he saw a man playing with his beard in prayer and said: 'Had his heart been humble, his limbs would have been humble.' Al-ʿAbath is an action with no benefit, interest, or wisdom requiring it. Imam Badr al-Din al-Kardari said: It is an action with a purpose that is not legal, while safah (foolishness) is an action with no purpose at all. Imam Hamid al-Din said: Al-ʿAbath is every action with no purpose. Shaykh Akmal al-Din said: There is no dispute in terminology. Al-Dayri said: What is mentioned in the commentaries of al-Hidayah and others: Al-ʿAbath is an action for an invalid purpose. The verification is that the intended meaning of ʿabath here is doing what is not from the actions of prayer, because it contradicts prayer. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed in prayer there is occupation' end. In Majmaʿ al-Riwayat: It is said in al-Badriyya: Prohibited things are four: al-ʿabath, al-safah, al-jahl, and al-zulm. The relation of ʿabath to safah is like the relation of jahl to zulm. For in safah and zulm there is harm (idrar), unlike ʿabath and jahl, for in them there is detriment (darar) without harm. Safah is stronger than ʿabath just as zulm is stronger than jahl. Al-ʿAbath is an action devoid of benefit; al-safah is that which entails harm. In al-Hidayah: Al-ʿAbath outside prayer is haram, so what do you think about it in prayer? And in al-Humaydi: Al-ʿAbath is haram due to his saying (peace be upon him):
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, typical of the Hanafi school. It begins by defining the term 'makruh' and distinguishing its two levels: tanzihi (lightly disliked) and tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). A makruh tanzihi is where abandonment is preferred but the act is not sinful, while makruh tahrimi is closer to haram and requires a speculative prohibition (nahy zanni). The commentary then clarifies that despite the dislike, the prayer remains valid because its essential conditions are met; however, it should be repeated in a non-disliked manner as a precaution. This ruling applies universally to any prayer performed with dislike. The author addresses a potential contradiction with a hadith that might suggest not repeating a prayer, but explains that hadith refers to repetition due to waswasa, not due to dislike. The passage then lists approximately seventy-seven disliked things, beginning with the universal principle that intentionally omitting a wajib or sunnah act is disliked. It provides examples such as lacking tranquility in pillars, racing the imam (citing a strong hadith warning), and various physical actions like passing hands beyond ears or placing them below shoulders. A significant portion is devoted to the concept of 'abath (frivolous action), defined as an action with no legitimate purpose, which contradicts khushu' (humility), the spirit of prayer. The commentary reviews different scholarly definitions, concluding that 'abath in prayer means doing anything not from the acts of prayer. It is deemed disliked or even haram based on hadith and Quranic verses. This analysis is firmly rooted in the Hanafi tradition, with references to key works like al-Hidayah and the rulings of Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action whose abandonment is preferable to its performance; may be tanzihi or tahrimi.
عبث (ʿabath): An action with no legitimate purpose or benefit; in prayer, any act not from the actions of prayer that contradicts khushuʿ.
خشوع (khushuʿ): Humility and focus in prayer, considered its spirit; its opposite is frivolity (ʿabath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the verified meaning of 'abath in prayer?
A) Any action with no purpose at all.
B) Any action done for an invalid purpose.
C) Any action not from the actions of prayer.
D) Any action that causes harm to others.

Key Takeaway
The disliked acts of prayer are many, but the core principle is that any action contradicting khushu' is disliked; 'abath is a prime example.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Ruling of 'Abath (Futility) in Prayer
Defines abath, provides proofs, and gives examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'abath in prayer, identify the evidence that supports it, and distinguish 'abath from safah.

Core Idea
'Abath in prayer is prohibited because it destroys khushu', the spirit of salah.

This lesson defines 'abath (futility) and explains its prohibition in prayer according to the Hanafi school. We will examine the textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, understand why 'abath contradicts khushu', and learn the precise legal ruling. The passage also distinguishes 'abath from safah (foolishness) and lists common examples of 'abath in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what 'abath means and what hukm (legal classification) it carries in the context of prayer. The text uses both 'makruh' and 'haram' – note the nuance.
The passage initially calls it makruh but later quotes al-Badriyya calling it haram; Hanafi fatwa settles on makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the Quranic verse and multiple hadith cited. The Quranic command for khushu' and the explicit prohibition in hadith are the primary proofs.
Hadith include: 'Allah dislikes for you futility in prayer', 'Restrain your hands in prayer', and the story of the man playing with his beard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Explain how each proof leads to the prohibition. The Quranic verse implies that actions destroying khushu' are forbidden; the hadith directly prohibit 'abath.
The imperative 'kufu aydiyakum' (restrain your hands) indicates prohibition (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (difference of opinion)
Understand that there is a disagreement about the severity: some Hanafi sources call it haram, others makruh tahrimi. Also note that outside prayer, 'abath is explicitly haram.
Al-Hidayah states: 'Abath outside prayer is haram, so what do you think of it in prayer?' This strengthens the case for prohibition inside.
5
Apply the definition to examples
Recognize concrete instances of 'abath mentioned in the text: turning pebbles, cracking fingers, intertwining fingers, resting on hips (takhassur).
Exception: turning pebbles once for prostration is allowed, as it has a valid purpose.

كعَبَيْهِ بثوبه، وبدنه . (۲) الكلي المنطبق على جزئيات كثيرة، كـ ترك الاطمئنان في الأركان، وكـ مسابقة الإمام، لما فيها من الوعيد على ما في الصحيحين: ( أمَا يَخْشَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِذَا رَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ رَأْسَهُ رَأْسَ حِمَارٍ أَوْ يَجْعَلَ صُورَتَهُ صُورَةَ حِمَارٍ » (1) وكمجاوزة اليدين الأذنين، وجعلهما تحت المنكبين، وستر القدمين في السجود عمداً للرجال، (كعبيه بثوبه، وبدنهِ لأن العبث ينافي الخشوع الذي هو روح الصلاة، فكان مكروهاً لقوله تعالى: (قَدْ أَفْلَحَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ ) الَّذِينَ هُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ خَشِعُونَ ( ) الو ] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ الله كَرِهَ لَكُمْ العَبَثَ فِي الصَّلاةِ، وَالرَّفَثَ فِي الصَّيَامِ، والضَحِكَ عِنْدَ المَقَابِرِ » (٣) وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «كُفُوا أَيْدِيَكُمْ فِي الصَّلاةِ » (۳) ورأى عليه الصلاة والسلام رجلاً يعبث بلحيته في الصَّلاةِ فقال : ( لو خَشَعَ قَلْبُهُ لَخَشَعَتْ جوارحه ) والعبث: عبارة عن عمل لا فائدة فيه، ولا مصلحة ولا حكمة تقتضيه، وقال الإمام بدر الدين الكردري: إنه فعل فيه غرض ليس بشرعي، والسفه ما لا غرض فيه أصلاً. وقال الإمام حميد الدين: الـعـبـث كـل عمل ليس فيه غرض ، وقال الشيخ أكمل الدين ولا نزاع في الاصطلاح، وقال الديـــري: المذكور في شروح الهداية» وغيرها: إن العبث الفعل لغرض غير صحيح، والتحقيق أن المراد بالعبث ها هنا: فعل ما ليس من أفعال الصلاة، لأنه ينافي الصلاة. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ فِي الصَّلاةِ شُغلا (٥) انتهى. وفي مجمع الروايات»: قال في «البدرية ) : : المحرمات أربعة: العبث، والسفه، والجهل، والظلم، ونسبة العبث إلى السفه كنسبة الجهل إلى الظلم. فإن في السفه والظلــم إضراراً دون العبث والجهل، فإن فيهما ضرراً لا إضراراً، والسفه أقوى من العبث كالظلم أقوى من الجهل، والعبث: عبارة عن فعل يخلو عن الفائدة، والسفه: عبارة عن ما يوجب المضرة، وفي « الهداية » : العبث خارج الصلاة حرام، فما ظنك به في الصلاة ، وفي ( الحميدي العبث حرام لقولـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام: (۱) أخرجه البخاري في الأذان، باب: إثم من رفع رأسه قبل الإمام (٦۹۱) ، واللفظ له ومسلم في الصلاة، باب: تحریم سبق الإمام بركوع أو سجود ونحوهما (٤٢٧). (٢) أخرجه القضاعي في مسند الشهاب (١٥٥/۲) ، والذهبي في ميزان الاعتدال (٤٠٢/١). (۳) لم أهتد إليه فيما بين يدي من كتب الحديث وإنما ذكره الفقهاء في كتبهم منهم الكاساني في البدائع (٢١٦/١). (٤) أخرجه الترمذي في نوادر الأصول (۲۱۰/۳)، وعبد الرزاق في مصنفه (٢٢٦/٢). Like his two heels with his garment and his body. (2) The general concept that applies to many particulars, like leaving tranquility in the pillars, and like preceding the Imam, due to the threat in the two Sahihs: 'Does not one of you fear, when he raises his head before the Imam, that Allah will make his head the head of a donkey or make his form the form of a donkey?' And like passing the hands beyond the ears, and placing them below the shoulders, and covering the feet in prostration deliberately for men, (his heels with his garment and his body) because 'abath (futility) contradicts khushu' which is the spirit of prayer, so it is makruh due to the saying of the Exalted: 'Successful indeed are the believers who are in their prayers khashi'un' and his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah has disliked for you futility in prayer, obscenity in fasting, and laughter at graves' and his saying, peace be upon him: 'Restrain your hands in prayer' and he saw a man playing with his beard in prayer and said: 'If his heart were humble, his limbs would be humble.' And 'abath is an action with no benefit, no interest, and no wisdom requiring it. Imam Badr al-Din al-Kardari said: It is an action with a non-legal purpose, while safah (foolishness) has no purpose at all. Imam Hamid al-Din said: 'Abath is every action without purpose. Shaykh Akmal al-Din said there is no dispute in terminology. Al-Dayri said: Mentioned in the commentaries of al-Hidayah and others: 'Abath is an action for an invalid purpose. The verification is that what is meant by 'abath here is doing what is not from the actions of prayer, because it contradicts prayer. He said, peace be upon him: 'Indeed in prayer there is occupation.' End. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: He said in al-Badriyya: The forbidden are four: 'abath, safah, ignorance, and oppression. The relation of 'abath to safah is like that of ignorance to oppression. For in safah and oppression there is harm, unlike 'abath and ignorance, for in them there is harm but no injuriousness. Safah is stronger than 'abath, just as oppression is stronger than ignorance. 'Abath is an action devoid of benefit, and safah is that which causes harm. In al-Hidayah: 'Abath outside prayer is haram, so what do you think of it in prayer? And in al-Humaydi: 'Abath is haram due to his saying, peace be upon him: (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari... End. And turning the pebbles, except for prostration once, and cracking the fingers, and intertwining them, and resting on the hips. He extends it until (4) 'I am not of ludicrous play nor is ludicrous play from me' (1) ludicrous play is amusement. End.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the concept of 'abath (futility) in prayer. The text begins by defining 'abath as a general concept encompassing many particular actions, such as leaving tranquility (itminan) in the obligatory acts of prayer, and racing the Imam in movements. It provides hadith evidence, including the famous threat against raising one's head before the Imam. The core ruling is that 'abath contradicts khushu' (humility and focus), which is the spirit of the prayer, and is therefore makruh (disliked), with some scholars holding it haram based on evidence like the hadith 'Allah has disliked for you futility in prayer.' The text then presents various scholarly definitions of 'abath: Imam Badr al-Din al-Kardari defines it as an action with a non-shar'i purpose, distinguishing it from safah (foolishness) which has no purpose at all. Imam Hamid al-Din defines it as any action without purpose. The author concludes that in this context, 'abath means any action not part of the prayer, because it opposes the very essence of prayer. The passage also mentions that 'abath outside prayer is haram, so its prohibition in prayer is even more severe. Finally, the text lists tangible examples of 'abath in prayer: turning pebbles (except for prostration once), cracking fingers, intertwining fingers, and resting hands on hips (takhassur). The hadith 'I am not of ludicrous play' reinforces the prohibition of frivolity.

Key Terms
العبث (al-‘abath): An action without benefit, purpose, or wisdom; in prayer, any action not part of the prayer's proper form.
الخشوع (al-khushū‘): Humility and focused devotion in prayer; the spirit of salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on 'abath (futility) performed during prayer?
A) Permissible (mubah) because it does not invalidate the prayer.
B) Makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) as it reduces reward but is not sinful.
C) Makruh tahrimi or haram (prohibitively disliked or forbidden) because it contradicts khushu'.
D) Recommended (sunnah) to avoid distraction.

Key Takeaway
'Abath in prayer is prohibited because it destroys khushu'; relying on explicit Quranic and hadith evidence, the Hanafi school rules it makruh tahrimi (and outside prayer, haram).
